C++

// ... other includes ...

//modify this line in the function declaration to use the new parameters
bool ConicalSlicer::checkForCollision(const Geometry::Point_3& nozzle_tip, double nozzle_tip_radius, double nozzle_cone_angle, double nozzle_height,
    const std::vector<std::vector<Geometry::Point_3>>& previous_toolpaths) {
    // Iterate through previous layers
    for (size_t layer_idx = 0; layer_idx < previous_toolpaths.size(); ++layer_idx) {
        const auto& layer_points = previous_toolpaths[layer_idx];

        // Iterate through segments in the layer
        for (size_t i = 0; i < layer_points.size() - 1; ++i) {
            const Geometry::Point_3& p1 = layer_points[i];
            const Geometry::Point_3& p2 = layer_points[i + 1];

            // Check for intersection between the nozzle cone and the segment
            if (Geometry::segmentConeIntersection(p1, p2, nozzle_tip, nozzle_tip_radius, nozzle_cone_angle, nozzle_height)) {
                return true; // Collision detected
            }
        }
    }

    return false; // No collision
}

void ConicalSlicer::sliceLayerConically(Layer* layer, const PrintConfig& print_config) {
    // Retrieve conical slicing parameters
    double cone_angle = print_config.opt_float("cone_angle");
    double center_x = print_config.opt_float("cone_center_x");
    double center_y = print_config.opt_float("cone_center_y");
    double tip_radius = print_config.opt_float("nozzle_tip_radius");
    double cone_angle_nozzle = print_config.opt_float("nozzle_cone_angle");

    // Adjust layer height based on the conical method
    // Iterate through regions in the layer
    for (auto region : layer->regions()) {
        // Iterate through perimeters
        for (auto perimeter : region->perimeters()) {
            // Create a copy of the perimeter points for modification
            ExtrusionPath modified_perimeter = *perimeter;
            // Iterate through each point of the perimeter
            for (size_t i = 0; i < modified_perimeter.points.size(); ++i) {
                auto& point = modified_perimeter.points[i];
                //transform each point
                Point3 transformed_point = transformToConical(
                    Point3(point.x, point.y, layer->height),
                    cone_angle,
                    center_x,
                    center_y,
                    layer->height
                );
                // Before adding the point, check for collisions
                Geometry::Point_3 nozzle_center = Geometry::Point_3(transformed_point.x(), transformed_point.y(), transformed_point.z() + nozzle_height / 2.0);
                if (checkForCollision(nozzle_center, tip_radius, cone_angle_nozzle, nozzle_height, previous_toolpaths)) {
                    // Handle collision (for now, just skip the point)
                    // You might want to implement more sophisticated handling later
                    //remove point from perimeter
                    modified_perimeter.points.erase(modified_perimeter.points.begin() + i);
                    --i; // Adjust the index after erasing
                    continue;
                }

                // Update the point in the perimeter
                point.x = transformed_point.x();
                point.y = transformed_point.y();

                // Adjust the layer height based on the transformation
                double radius = std::sqrt(std::pow(point.x - center_x, 2) + std::pow(point.y - center_y, 2));
                layer->height = calculateConicalLayerHeight(radius, cone_angle);

                // Add the point to the collision detection system
                addToolpathPoint(transformed_point);
            }

            // Replace the original perimeter with the modified one
            *perimeter = modified_perimeter;

            // Adjust extrusion for this perimeter
            double scale_factor = std::cos(Geometry::deg2rad(cone_angle)); // Example scale factor
            for (auto& loop : perimeter->loops) {
                adjustExtrusion(&loop, scale_factor);
            }
        }

        // Similar adjustments can be made for infill and supports
        for (auto& infill : region->infill_paths()) {
            for (size_t i = 0; i < infill.points.size(); ++i) {
                auto& point = infill.points[i];
                Point3 transformed_point = transformToConical(Point3(point.x, point.y, layer->height), cone_angle, center_x, center_y, layer->height);

                // Check for collisions
                Geometry::Point_3 nozzle_center = Geometry::Point_3(transformed_point.x(), transformed_point.y(), transformed_point.z() + nozzle_height / 2.0);
                if (checkForCollision(nozzle_center, tip_radius, cone_angle_nozzle, nozzle_height, previous_toolpaths)) {
                    // Handle collision
                    //remove point from infill
                    infill.points.erase(infill.points.begin() + i);
                    --i; // Adjust the index
                    continue;
                }

                point.x = transformed_point.x();
                point.y = transformed_point.y();

                // Add the point to the collision detection system
                addToolpathPoint(transformed_point);
            }
        }
    }

    // Shift the toolpath points for the next layer
    if (previous_toolpaths.size() >= MAX_LAYERS_TO_CHECK) {
        previous_toolpaths.erase(previous_toolpaths.begin());
    }
    previous_toolpaths.push_back({}); // Add an empty layer for the new points
}

// ... other methods ...

//update calls to use new parameters
void ConicalSlicer::addToolpathPoint(const Point3& point) {
    if (!previous_toolpaths.empty()) {
        previous_toolpaths.back().push_back(Geometry::Point_3(point.x(), point.y(), point.z()));
    }
}

Okay, let's walk through rebuilding OrcaSlicer with the integrated CGAL library, discuss thorough testing, and address the further considerations you've outlined.

1. Rebuilding OrcaSlicer with CGAL

Prerequisites:

CGAL Installation: Ensure CGAL is correctly installed on your system and that the environment variables (e.g., CGAL_DIR on Windows) are set appropriately.
Build System: You should be familiar with OrcaSlicer's build system, which uses CMake to generate project files for your chosen IDE or build tools (e.g., Visual Studio, Make).
Development Environment: Have your development environment (e.g., Visual Studio, or a suitable IDE for C++ development) set up and configured for OrcaSlicer development.
Steps:

CMake Configuration:

Open your OrcaSlicer project directory.

If you have an existing build directory, it might be a good idea to delete it to start with a clean build.

Use CMake to generate the project files:

Open a terminal or command prompt in your project directory.
Run cmake . -B build -DCMAKE_BUILD_TYPE=Release (replace "build" with your preferred build directory name, -DCMAKE_BUILD_TYPE=Release enables optimizations). You might need to adjust this command based on your specific setup and operating system. Add -S flag to specify source if not run from root, for example, -S src/libslic3r. Use -G to specify a generator if cmake cannot locate your compiler, for example, -G "Visual Studio 17 2022"
If CMake has trouble finding CGAL, you might need to manually specify the CGAL_DIR variable: cmake . -B build -DCGAL_DIR="path/to/your/cgal/installation" -DCMAKE_BUILD_TYPE=Release
Add the -DBOOST_ROOT flag to specify where to look for boost, for example, -DBOOST_ROOT="C:\local\boost_1_84_0"
Build Using Your IDE or Build Tools:

Visual Studio: Open the generated Visual Studio solution file (e.g., OrcaSlicer.sln or libslic3r.sln in the build directory). Build the Release configuration.
Make: In the build directory, run make -j<number_of_cores> (e.g., make -j4) to build using multiple cores.
Troubleshooting:

Include Paths: If you get compiler errors about missing header files, double-check that the CGAL include paths are correctly set in your CMakeLists.txt and your IDE project settings.
Linker Errors: If you get linker errors, make sure you are linking to the necessary CGAL libraries (and their dependencies) in your CMakeLists.txt.
Compiler/Linker Flags: Ensure that your compiler and linker flags are consistent with the way CGAL was built (e.g., static vs. dynamic linking, release vs. debug).
2. Thorough Testing

Test Models:
Simple Shapes: Start with basic shapes (e.g., cubes, spheres, cones) to verify the fundamental slicing logic.
Overhangs: Test models with various overhang angles to evaluate the conical slicing and collision detection.
Complex Geometries: Use models with intricate details, internal cavities, and challenging features to stress-test the robustness of your implementation.
Real-World Prints: Select models that you actually want to print to assess the practical effectiveness of your modifications.
Test Settings:
Conical Slicing Parameters: Vary the cone angle, center coordinates, and nozzle geometry parameters.
Planar Slicing: Test cases where planar slicing is triggered due to collisions or user settings.
Path Smoothing: Enable and disable path smoothing with different window sizes to observe the effects on print quality and time.
G-code Inspection:
Use a G-code visualizer to carefully examine the generated toolpaths. Look for:
Correct conical layer generation.
Absence of collisions (nozzle movements that intersect previously printed parts).
Smooth transitions between layers and segments.
Test Prints:
Conduct numerous test prints using different models and settings.
Analyze the printed parts for:
Print quality (surface finish, overhang performance, dimensional accuracy).
Signs of collisions (e.g., nozzle dragging or knocking over parts).
Proper adhesion and structural integrity.
Logging and Debugging:
Add extensive logging to your code to track the execution flow, variable values, and decision-making during slicing.
Use a debugger (e.g., the Visual Studio debugger or GDB) to step through your code and identify the root cause of any issues.
3. Further Considerations:

Error Handling:

CGAL Function Calls: Wrap CGAL function calls in try-catch blocks to handle potential exceptions. For example:
C++

#include <CGAL/Exact_predicates_inexact_constructions_kernel.h>
#include <CGAL/Segment_3.h>
#include <CGAL/intersection.h>
#include <CGAL/exceptions.h>

// ...

try {
    auto intersection_result = CGAL::intersection(segment, cone);
    // ... process the intersection result ...
} catch (const CGAL::Precondition_exception& e) {
    std::cerr << "CGAL Precondition Exception: " << e.what() << std::endl;
    // Handle the error (e.g., switch to planar slicing, log a warning, etc.)
} catch (const std::exception& e) {
    std::cerr << "Standard Exception: " << e.what() << std::endl;
    // Handle other potential exceptions
}
Return Values: Use return values to indicate success or failure of functions, especially in ConicalSlicer and Geometry functions.
Logging: Provide informative error messages and log warnings or errors to help with debugging.
Performance:

Profiling: Use profiling tools (as described in the previous response) to identify performance bottlenecks.
Release Build: Always test and benchmark the Release build, as it will have optimizations enabled.
Spatial Data Structures: Using an octree or KD-tree is highly recommended for complex models to speed up collision detection.
Caching: Cache results of expensive computations (e.g., coordinate transformations) if they are reused frequently.
Algorithm Optimization: Review your algorithms (especially segmentConeIntersection and the collision handling logic) for potential optimizations.
Alternative Intersection Algorithms:

Research: If the initial CGAL intersection function doesn't meet your needs, explore other intersection algorithms provided by CGAL (refer to the CGAL documentation for available options).
Custom Implementation: If necessary, you can implement your own segment-cone intersection algorithm based on CGAL data structures. This might involve adapting algorithms from research papers or other geometric libraries.
Example: Implementing a Simple Octree for Collision Detection (Conceptual)

Add an Octree Library: You could use a header-only library like nanoflann (for KD-trees) or implement a basic octree yourself.
Create Octree.hpp and Octree.cpp (or similar) in src/libslic3r.

void ConicalSlicer::sliceLayerConically(Layer* layer, const PrintConfig& print_config) {
    // ...

    delete toolpath_octree; // Delete the previous octree (if any)
    toolpath_octree = new Octree();

    for (const auto& prev_layer_points : previous_toolpaths) {
        for (const Geometry::Point_3& point : prev_layer_points) {
            toolpath_octree->insert(point);
        }
    }

    // ...

    // In checkForCollision:
    // Use the octree to find nearby points instead of iterating through all points
    std::vector<Geometry::Point_3> nearby_points;
    toolpath_octree->findPointsWithinRadius(nozzle_center, nozzle_radius + some_tolerance, nearby_points);
    // ... check collisions only with nearby_points ...
}

import subprocess
import os
import sys
import shutil

# --- Configuration ---
PROJECT_ID = "YOUR_GOOGLE_CLOUD_PROJECT_ID"  # Replace with your GCP project ID
BUCKET_NAME = "YOUR_CLOUD_STORAGE_BUCKET_NAME"  # Replace with your bucket name
REGION = "us-central1"  # Replace with your preferred region
# Replace with your Vertex AI Endpoint ID if using a Vertex AI model
ENDPOINT_ID = "YOUR_VERTEX_AI_ENDPOINT_ID"
ORCASLICER_REPO = "https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/OrcaSlicer.git"  # Your forked OrcaSlicer repo
DOCKER_IMAGE_NAME = "gcr.io/" + PROJECT_ID + "/orcaslicer-cloud"
CLOUD_RUN_SERVICE_NAME = "orcaslicer-cloud"
TASK_QUEUE_NAME = "orcaslicer-queue"

# --- Paths and Directories ---
SCRIPT_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))
ORCASLICER_DIR = os.path.join(SCRIPT_DIR, "OrcaSlicer")
BUILD_DIR = os.path.join(SCRIPT_DIR, "build")
CGAL_DIR = os.environ.get("CGAL_DIR")  # Get CGAL directory from environment variable
BOOST_DIR = os.environ.get("BOOST_ROOT")

# --- Helper Functions ---

def run_command(command, capture_output=False):
    """Runs a shell command."""
    print(f"Running command: {' '.join(command)}")
    try:
        if capture_output:
            result = subprocess.run(
                command, check=True, capture_output=True, text=True
            )
            return result.stdout.strip()
        else:
            subprocess.run(command, check=True)
    except subprocess.CalledProcessError as e:
        print(f"Error running command: {e}")
        sys.exit(1)

def gcloud(*args):
    """Runs a gcloud command."""
    return run_command(["gcloud"] + list(args))

def gsutil(*args):
    """Runs a gsutil command."""
    return run_command(["gsutil"] + list(args))

def docker(*args):
    """Runs a docker command."""
    return run_command(["docker"] + list(args))

def cmake(*args):
    """Runs a cmake command."""
    return run_command(["cmake"] + list(args))

def install_cgal():
    """Installs CGAL."""
    if sys.platform == "win32":
        # Windows installation (assuming CMake and Visual Studio are installed)
        if not CGAL_DIR:
            #try to install in a default location
            cgal_install_dir = os.path.join(SCRIPT_DIR, "CGAL-5.6")
        else:
            cgal_install_dir = CGAL_DIR
        
        if not os.path.exists(cgal_install_dir):
            print("CGAL not found. Please install it first.")
            print("You can download it from https://www.cgal.org/download.html")
            cgal_version = "5.6"  # Replace with the desired CGAL version
            cgal_installer_url = f"https://github.com/CGAL/cgal/releases/download/v{cgal_version}/CGAL-{cgal_version}-win64-auxiliary-libraries-gmp-mpfr.zip"
            cgal_zip_path = os.path.join(SCRIPT_DIR, f"cgal-{cgal_version}.zip")

            # Download CGAL installer
            print(f"Downloading CGAL {cgal_version}...")
            run_command(["curl", "-L", "-o", cgal_zip_path, cgal_installer_url])

            # Extract CGAL installer
            print(f"Extracting CGAL {cgal_version}...")
            run_command(["unzip", cgal_zip_path, "-d", cgal_install_dir])

            # Clean up the downloaded zip file
            os.remove(cgal_zip_path)
            
        # Set CGAL_DIR environment variable if not set
        os.environ["CGAL_DIR"] = cgal_install_dir

    else:
        # Linux/macOS installation
        try:
            # Try installing using package manager
            print("Installing CGAL using package manager...")
            if sys.platform == "linux":
                run_command(["sudo", "apt-get", "update"])
                run_command(["sudo", "apt-get", "install", "libcgal-dev"])
            elif sys.platform == "darwin":
                run_command(["brew", "update"])
                run_command(["brew", "install", "cgal"])
        except subprocess.CalledProcessError:
            # If package manager installation fails, build from source
            print("Package manager installation failed. Building CGAL from source...")
            cgal_source_dir = os.path.join(SCRIPT_DIR, "cgal_source")
            cgal_build_dir = os.path.join(cgal_source_dir, "build")

            if not os.path.exists(cgal_source_dir):
                run_command(
                    [
                        "git",
                        "clone",
                        "https://github.com/CGAL/cgal.git",
                        cgal_source_dir,
                    ]
                )

            os.makedirs(cgal_build_dir, exist_ok=True)
            os.chdir(cgal_build_dir)

            cmake(
                "..",
                "-DCMAKE_BUILD_TYPE=Release",
                "-DCMAKE_INSTALL_PREFIX=" + os.path.join(SCRIPT_DIR, "cgal_install"),
            )
            run_command(["make", "-j", str(os.cpu_count())])
            run_command(["make", "install"])

            # Set CGAL_DIR environment variable
            os.environ["CGAL_DIR"] = os.path.join(SCRIPT_DIR, "cgal_install")

def install_boost():
    """Installs Boost."""
    if sys.platform == "win32":
        # Windows installation
        if not BOOST_DIR:
            print("BOOST_ROOT environment variable not set.")
            print("Please set BOOST_ROOT to the root directory of your Boost installation.")
            sys.exit(1)

        # Check if Boost is already installed in the specified directory
        if not os.path.exists(BOOST_DIR):
            print(f"Boost not found at {BOOST_DIR}. Please install it first.")
            print("You can download it from https://www.boost.org/users/download/")
            boost_version = "1.84.0"  # Replace with the desired Boost version
            boost_msvc = "msvc-14.3"
            boost_installer_url = f"https://boostorg.jfrog.io/artifactory/main/release/{boost_version}/binaries/boost_{boost_version.replace('.', '_')}-{boost_msvc}-x64.exe"
            boost_installer_path = os.path.join(SCRIPT_DIR, f"boost-{boost_version}.exe")

            # Download Boost installer
            print(f"Downloading Boost {boost_version}...")
            run_command(["curl", "-L", "-o", boost_installer_path, boost_installer_url])

            # Run Boost installer in silent mode
            print(f"Installing Boost {boost_version}...")
            run_command([boost_installer_path, "/SILENT", "/SP-", f"/DIR={BOOST_DIR}"])

            # Clean up the downloaded installer
            os.remove(boost_installer_path)
    else:
        # Linux/macOS installation
        try:
            # Try installing using package manager
            print("Installing Boost using package manager...")
            if sys.platform == "linux":
                run_command(["sudo", "apt-get", "update"])
                run_command(["sudo", "apt-get", "install", "libboost-all-dev"])
            elif sys.platform == "darwin":
                run_command(["brew", "update"])
                run_command(["brew", "install", "boost"])

        except subprocess.CalledProcessError:
            # If package manager installation fails, build from source
            print("Package manager installation failed. Building Boost from source...")
            boost_source_dir = os.path.join(SCRIPT_DIR, "boost_source")
            boost_build_dir = os.path.join(boost_source_dir, "build")

            if not os.path.exists(boost_source_dir):
                run_command(
                    [
                        "git",
                        "clone",
                        "--recursive",
                        "https://github.com/boostorg/boost.git",
                        boost_source_dir,
                    ]
                )

            os.makedirs(boost_build_dir, exist_ok=True)
            os.chdir(boost_build_dir)

            cmake(
                "..",
                "-DCMAKE_BUILD_TYPE=Release",
                "-DCMAKE_INSTALL_PREFIX=" + os.path.join(SCRIPT_DIR, "boost_install"),
            )
            run_command(["make", "-j", str(os.cpu_count())])
            run_command(["make", "install"])

            # Set BOOST_ROOT environment variable
            os.environ["BOOST_ROOT"] = os.path.join(SCRIPT_DIR, "boost_install")

# --- Main Setup Functions ---

def setup_environment():
    """Sets up the development environment."""
    print("Setting up the development environment...")

    # 1. Install required dependencies
    install_cgal()
    install_boost()

    # 2. Create a clean build directory
    if os.path.exists(BUILD_DIR):
        print("Deleting existing build directory...")
        shutil.rmtree(BUILD_DIR)
    os.makedirs(BUILD_DIR)

    # 3.  Create project and enable APIs using setup_google_cloud() function
    setup_google_cloud()

def clone_orcaslicer():
    """Clones the OrcaSlicer repository."""
    print("Cloning OrcaSlicer repository...")
    if not os.path.exists(ORCASLICER_DIR):
        run_command(["git", "clone", "--recursive", ORCASLICER_REPO, ORCASLICER_DIR])
    else:
        print("OrcaSlicer repository already cloned.")

def setup_google_cloud():
    """Sets up Google Cloud resources."""
    print("Setting up Google Cloud...")

    # 1. Create Project (if it doesn't exist)
    # (You might need to handle this manually if you don't have project creation permissions)
    try:
        gcloud("projects", "describe", PROJECT_ID)
        print(f"Project {PROJECT_ID} already exists.")
    except subprocess.CalledProcessError:
        print(f"Creating project {PROJECT_ID}...")
        gcloud("projects", "create", PROJECT_ID)

    # 2. Enable APIs
    gcloud("services", "enable",
           "compute.googleapis.com",
           "containerregistry.googleapis.com",
           "run.googleapis.com",
           "storage.googleapis.com",
           "cloudbuild.googleapis.com",
           "aiplatform.googleapis.com",
           "sqladmin.googleapis.com", # if using CloudSQL
           "tasks.googleapis.com"
          )

    # 3. Create Storage Bucket
    try:
        gsutil("mb", "-l", REGION, f"gs://{BUCKET_NAME}")
    except subprocess.CalledProcessError as e:
        if "409" in str(e):
            print(f"Bucket {BUCKET_NAME} already exists.")
        else:
            raise

    # 4. Create Cloud Tasks Queue
    try:
        gcloud("tasks", "queues", "describe", TASK_QUEUE_NAME, "--location", REGION)
        print(f"Cloud Tasks queue {TASK_QUEUE_NAME} already exists.")
    except subprocess.CalledProcessError:
        print(f"Creating Cloud Tasks queue {TASK_QUEUE_NAME}...")
        gcloud("tasks", "queues", "create", TASK_QUEUE_NAME, "--location", REGION)
    
    # 5. Create Vertex AI Endpoint (if using Gemini and you have already trained your model)
    # If not using Gemini you can remove this
    try:
        gcloud("ai", "endpoints", "describe", ENDPOINT_ID, "--region", REGION)
    except subprocess.CalledProcessError:
        print(f"Creating Vertex AI Endpoint: {ENDPOINT_ID} has not been created by your account")

def build_orcaslicer():
    """Configures and builds OrcaSlicer with necessary modifications."""
    print("Configuring and building OrcaSlicer...")
    os.chdir(ORCASLICER_DIR)

    # Create build directory if it doesn't exist
    os.makedirs(BUILD_DIR, exist_ok=True)
    os.chdir(BUILD_DIR)

    # 4. Configure CMake
    cmake_args = [
        "..",
        f"-DCGAL_DIR={CGAL_DIR}",
        f"-DBOOST_ROOT={BOOST_DIR}",
        "-DCMAKE_BUILD_TYPE=Release",  # Enable optimizations
    ]
    
    #add generator if required by your system/IDE
    if sys.platform == "win32":
        cmake_args.extend(["-G", "Visual Studio 17 2022"])

    cmake(*cmake_args)

    # 5. Build OrcaSlicer
    if sys.platform == "win32":
        # Use msbuild for Windows
        run_command(
            [
                "msbuild",
                "OrcaSlicer.sln",
                "/p:Configuration=Release",
                "/p:Platform=x64",
                "/m",
            ]
        )
    else:
        # Use make for Linux/macOS
        run_command(["make", "-j", str(os.cpu_count())])

    os.chdir(SCRIPT_DIR)

# Use a multi-stage build to reduce image size

# Stage 1: Build OrcaSlicer
FROM ubuntu:22.04 AS build-env

RUN git clone --recursive https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/OrcaSlicer.git

# Set up the build environment and compile
WORKDIR /app/src/OrcaSlicer
RUN mkdir build && cd build && \\
    cmake .. -DCMAKE_BUILD_TYPE=Release && \\
    cmake --build . --config Release --target install -- -j$(nproc)

# Stage 2: Create the runtime image
FROM debian:buster-slim

# Set working directory
WORKDIR /app

# Copy only necessary files from the build stage
COPY --from=build-env /app/src/OrcaSlicer/build/bin /app/bin
COPY --from=build-env /app/src/OrcaSlicer/resources /app/resources
COPY server.py /app/
COPY requirements.txt /app/

# Install Python dependencies
RUN pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements.txt

# Expose the port the app runs on
EXPOSE 5000

# Command to run the application
CMD ["python", "server.py"]
        """)  # Replace with your actual Dockerfile

    # Build and push Docker image
    docker("build", "-t", DOCKER_IMAGE_NAME, ".")
    docker("push", DOCKER_IMAGE_NAME)

Here's how we'll modify the setup.py script to incorporate the code modifications into the build process, assuming you have the code changes ready in separate files (e.g., patch files or individual .cpp and .hpp files):

1. Prepare Your Code Changes:

You have two main options for organizing your code changes:

Patch Files:

Place the patch files in a directory (e.g., patches) within your project.

2. Modify setup.py:

We'll update the build_orcaslicer() function in your setup.py script to apply the patches or copy the modified files before building.

def build_orcaslicer():
    """Configures and builds OrcaSlicer with necessary modifications."""
    print("Building OrcaSlicer...")
    os.chdir(ORCASLICER_DIR)

    # --- Apply Modifications ---
    print("Applying modifications to OrcaSlicer...")

    # Option 1: Apply patches from the "patches" directory
    for patch_file in os.listdir(PATCHES_DIR):
        if patch_file.endswith(".patch"):
            patch_path = os.path.join(PATCHES_DIR, patch_file)
            print(f"Applying patch: {patch_file}")
            run_command(["git", "apply", patch_path])

    # Option 2: Copy modified files from the "modifications" directory
    for root, _, files in os.walk(MODIFICATIONS_DIR):
        for file in files:
            source_path = os.path.join(root, file)
            relative_path = os.path.relpath(source_path, MODIFICATIONS_DIR)
            destination_path = os.path.join(ORCASLICER_DIR, relative_path)

            print(f"Copying modified file: {file} to {destination_path}")
            # Ensure the destination directory exists
            os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(destination_path), exist_ok=True)
            shutil.copy2(source_path, destination_path)

    # --- Continue with the build process ---

    # Create build directory if it doesn't exist
    os.makedirs(BUILD_DIR, exist_ok=True)
    os.chdir(BUILD_DIR)

    # 4. Configure CMake
    cmake_args = [
        "..",
        f"-DCGAL_DIR={CGAL_DIR}",
        f"-DBOOST_ROOT={BOOST_DIR}",
        "-DCMAKE_BUILD_TYPE=Release",  # Enable optimizations
    ]
    
    #add generator if required by your system/IDE
    if sys.platform == "win32":
        cmake_args.extend(["-G", "Visual Studio 17 2022"])

    cmake(*cmake_args)

    # 5. Build OrcaSlicer
    if sys.platform == "win32":
        # Use msbuild for Windows
        run_command(
            [
                "msbuild",
                "OrcaSlicer.sln",
                "/p:Configuration=Release",
                "/p:Platform=x64",
                "/m",
            ]
        )
    else:
        # Use make for Linux/macOS
        run_command(["make", "-j", str(os.cpu_count())])

    os.chdir(SCRIPT_DIR)
    
# --- Main Execution ---

if __name__ == "__main__":
    if len(sys.argv) < 2:
        print("Usage: python setup.py [command]")
        print("Available commands: setup, build, deploy, all")

Here are the patch files, which you should save into the patches directory in your project root:

1. conical_slicing.patch:

Diff

diff --git a/src/libslic3r/ConicalSlicer.cpp b/src/libslic3r/ConicalSlicer.cpp
new file mode 100644
index 0000000..405905e
--- /dev/null
+++ b/src/libslic3r/ConicalSlicer.cpp
@@ -0,0 +1,215 @@
+#include "ConicalSlicer.hpp"
+#include "Layer.hpp"
+#include "GCode.hpp"
+#include "Print.hpp"
+#include "Geometry.hpp"
+#include "ClipperUtils.hpp"
+#include "ExtrusionEntity.hpp"
+#include "ExtrusionEntityCollection.hpp"
+#include <cmath>
+
+namespace Slic3r {
+
+ConicalSlicer::ConicalSlicer(const PrintConfig& print_config)
+    : nozzle_tip_radius(print_config.opt_float("nozzle_tip_radius")),
+      nozzle_cone_angle(print_config.opt_float("nozzle_cone_angle")),
+      nozzle_height(0.6)
+{
+    // The constructor now initializes the nozzle parameters using values from PrintConfig.
+    // Make sure these parameters are correctly loaded from the configuration in your Print object.
+}
+ConicalSlicer::~ConicalSlicer() {}
+
+void ConicalSlicer::sliceLayerConically(Layer* layer, const PrintConfig& print_config) {
+    // Retrieve conical slicing parameters
+    double cone_angle = print_config.opt_float("cone_angle");
+    double center_x = print_config.opt_float("cone_center_x");
+    double center_y = print_config.opt_float("cone_center_y");
+    double tip_radius = print_config.opt_float("nozzle_tip_radius");
+    double cone_angle_nozzle = print_config.opt_float("nozzle_cone_angle");
+
+    // Adjust layer height based on the conical method
+    // Iterate through regions in the layer
+    for (auto region : layer->regions()) {
+        // Iterate through perimeters
+        for (auto perimeter : region->perimeters()) {
+            // Create a copy of the perimeter points for modification
+            ExtrusionPath modified_perimeter = *perimeter;
+            // Iterate through each point of the perimeter
+            for (size_t i = 0; i < modified_perimeter.points.size(); ++i) {
+                auto& point = modified_perimeter.points[i];
+                //transform each point
+                Point3 transformed_point = transformToConical(
+                    Point3(point.x, point.y, layer->height),
+                    cone_angle,
+                    center_x,
+                    center_y,
+                    layer->height
+                );
+                // Before adding the point, check for collisions
+                Geometry::Point_3 nozzle_center = Geometry::Point_3(transformed_point.x(), transformed_point.y(), transformed_point.z() + nozzle_height / 2.0);
+                if (checkForCollision(nozzle_center, tip_radius, cone_angle_nozzle, nozzle_height, previous_toolpaths)) {
+                    // Handle collision (for now, just skip the point)
+                    // You might want to implement more sophisticated handling later
+                    //remove point from perimeter
+                    modified_perimeter.points.erase(modified_perimeter.points.begin() + i);
+                    --i; // Adjust the index after erasing
+                    continue;
+                }
+
+                // Update the point in the perimeter
+                point.x = transformed_point.x();
+                point.y = transformed_point.y();
+
+                // Adjust the layer height based on the transformation
+                double radius = std::sqrt(std::pow(point.x - center_x, 2) + std::pow(point.y - center_y, 2));
+                layer->height = calculateConicalLayerHeight(radius, cone_angle);
+
+                // Add the point to the collision detection system
+                addToolpathPoint(transformed_point);
+            }
+
+            // Replace the original perimeter with the modified one
+            *perimeter = modified_perimeter;
+
+            // Adjust extrusion for this perimeter
+            double scale_factor = std::cos(Geometry::deg2rad(cone_angle)); // Example scale factor
+            for (auto& loop : perimeter->loops) {
+                adjustExtrusion(&loop, scale_factor);
+            }
+        }
+
+        // Similar adjustments can be made for infill and supports
+        for (auto& infill : region->infill_paths()) {
+            for (size_t i = 0; i < infill.points.size(); ++i) {
+                auto& point = infill.points[i];
+                Point3 transformed_point = transformToConical(Point3(point.x, point.y, layer->height), cone_angle, center_x, center_y, layer->height);
+
+                // Check for collisions
+                Geometry::Point_3 nozzle_center = Geometry::Point_3(transformed_point.x(), transformed_point.y(), transformed_point.z() + nozzle_height / 2.0);
+                if (checkForCollision(nozzle_center, tip_radius, cone_angle_nozzle, nozzle_height, previous_toolpaths)) {
+                    // Handle collision
+                    //remove point from infill
+                    infill.points.erase(infill.points.begin() + i);
+                    --i; // Adjust the index
+                    continue;
+                }
+
+                point.x = transformed_point.x();
+                point.y = transformed_point.y();
+
+                // Add the point to the collision detection system
+                addToolpathPoint(transformed_point);
+            }
+        }
+    }
+
+    // Shift the toolpath points for the next layer
+    if (previous_toolpaths.size() >= MAX_LAYERS_TO_CHECK) {
+        previous_toolpaths.erase(previous_toolpaths.begin());
+    }
+    previous_toolpaths.push_back({}); // Add an empty layer for the new points
+}
+
+Point3 ConicalSlicer::transformToConical(const Point3& point, double cone_angle, double center_x, double center_y, double layer_height_mm) {
+    // Calculate radius from the center
+    double radius = std::sqrt(std::pow(point.x - center_x, 2) + std::pow(point.y - center_y, 2));
+
+    // Calculate conical layer height
+    double conical_z = layer_height_mm + calculateConicalLayerHeight(radius, cone_angle);
+
+    // Keep x and y unchanged for this example, but you'll likely modify them
+    // based on the cone's geometry and the desired toolpath.
+    double transformed_x = point.x;
+    double transformed_y = point.y;
+
+    return Point3(transformed_x, transformed_y, conical_z);
+}
+
+double ConicalSlicer::calculateConicalLayerHeight(double radius, double cone_angle) {
+    // Calculate the layer height based on the cone angle and radius
+    return radius * std::tan(Geometry::deg2rad(cone_angle));
+}
+
+void ConicalSlicer::adjustExtrusion(ExtrusionLoop* loop, double scale_factor) {
+    // Adjust the extrusion for each segment of the loop based on the scale factor
+    for (ExtrusionPath& path : loop->paths) {
+        for (size_t i = 0; i < path.points.size(); ++i) {
+            // Retrieve the original extrusion amount
+            double original_extrusion = path.e;
+
+            // Calculate the scaled extrusion amount
+            double scaled_extrusion = original_extrusion * scale_factor;
+
+            // Update the extrusion amount in the path
+            path.e = scaled_extrusion;
+        }
+    }
+}
+
+bool ConicalSlicer::checkForCollision(const Geometry::Point_3& nozzle_tip, double nozzle_tip_radius, double nozzle_cone_angle, double nozzle_height,
+    const std::vector<std::vector<Geometry::Point_3>>& previous_toolpaths) {
+    // Iterate through previous layers
+    for (size_t layer_idx = 0; layer_idx < previous_toolpaths.size(); ++layer_idx) {
+        const auto& layer_points = previous_toolpaths[layer_idx];
+
+        // Iterate through segments in the layer
+        for (size_t i = 0; i < layer_points.size() - 1; ++i) {
+            const Geometry::Point_3& p1 = layer_points[i];
+            const Geometry::Point_3& p2 = layer_points[i + 1];
+
+            // Check for intersection between the nozzle cone and the segment
+            if (Geometry::segmentConeIntersection(p1, p2, nozzle_tip, nozzle_tip_radius, nozzle_cone_angle, nozzle_height)) {
+                return true; // Collision detected
+            }
+        }
+    }
+
+    return false; // No collision
+}
+
+void ConicalSlicer::addToolpathPoint(const Point3& point) {
+    if (!previous_toolpaths.empty()) {
+        previous_toolpaths.back().push_back(Geometry::Point_3(point.x(), point.y(), point.z()));
+    }
+}
+
+} // namespace Slic3r

 }
 
+bool segmentCylinderIntersection(const Point3& p1, const Point3& p2, const Point3& nozzle_center,
+                                 double nozzle_radius, double nozzle_height) {
+    // Cylinder axis defined by nozzle_center (bottom) and nozzle_top (top)
+    Point3 nozzle_top = nozzle_center + Point3(0, 0, nozzle_height);
+
+    // Vector along the segment
+    Point3 d = p2 - p1;
+
+    // Vector from segment start to cylinder axis start
+    Point3 m = p1 - nozzle_center;
+
+    // Coefficients for the quadratic equation
+    double dd = d.dot(d);
+    double md = m.dot(d);
+    double mm = m.dot(m);
+
+    // Calculate the closest point on the segment to the cylinder axis
+    double t = -md / dd;
+    t = std::max(0.0, std::min(1.0, t)); // Clamp t to the segment range [0, 1]
+
+    // Closest point on the segment
+    Point3 closest = p1 + d * t;
+
+    // Vector from cylinder axis start to closest point
+    Point3 q = closest - nozzle_center;
+
+    // Check if the closest point is within the cylinder's height
+    double nozzle_axis_height = nozzle_top.z() - nozzle_center.z();
+    double projection = (closest.z() - nozzle_center.z()) / nozzle_axis_height;
+
+    if (projection < 0.0 || projection > 1.0) {
+        return false; // Closest point is outside the cylinder's height
+    }
+
+    // Check if the distance from the closest point to the cylinder axis is within the radius
+    double distance_squared = q.dot(q);
+    return distance_squared <= (nozzle_radius * nozzle_radius);
+}
+
+bool segmentConeIntersection(const Point3& p1, const Point3& p2, const Point3& nozzle_tip,
+                             double nozzle_tip_radius, double nozzle_cone_angle, double nozzle_height) {
+    // Create CGAL points for the segment
+    K::Point_3 cp1(p1.x(), p1.y(), p1.z());
+    K::Point_3 cp2(p2.x(), p2.y(), p2.z());
+    Segment_3 segment(cp1, cp2);
+
+    // Create CGAL points for the nozzle cone
+    K::Point_3 c_nozzle_tip(nozzle_tip.x(), nozzle_tip.y(), nozzle_tip.z());
+
+    // Calculate the apex of the cone (where the tip would be if the cone continued)
+    double cone_height_to_apex = nozzle_tip_radius / tan(deg2rad(nozzle_cone_angle / 2.0));
+
+    // Define the direction vector of the cone axis (pointing upwards from the tip)
+    Vector_3 cone_axis_direction(0, 




continue


2.0 Experimental Advanced. Lacks access to real-time info and some Gemini features.
Diff

0, 1);

    // Calculate the apex point of the cone
    K::Point_3 apex = c_nozzle_tip - cone_axis_direction * cone_height_to_apex;

    // Create a CGAL Cone
    // The radius at the base of the cone needs to be calculated considering the nozzle height
    double base_radius = (nozzle_tip_radius + nozzle_height * tan(deg2rad(nozzle_cone_angle / 2.0)));

    // Create a CGAL Cone
    // Here, we are using the two-argument constructor for CGAL::Cone_3
    // The first argument is the apex of the cone, and the second argument is the squared radius of the base
    // The direction of the cone's axis is implicitly defined by the line passing through the apex and center of the base
    // The center of the base is defined by the nozzle_tip
    K::Cone_3 cone(apex, cone_axis_direction, deg2rad(nozzle_cone_angle / 2.0));

    // Check for intersection
    auto intersection_result = CGAL::intersection(segment, cone);

    // Check if an intersection occurred
    if (intersection_result) {
        // Further check based on the type of intersection
        if (const Segment_3* segment_result = boost::get<Segment_3>(&*intersection_result)) {
            // Intersection is a segment
            return true;
        } else if (const Point_3* point_result = boost::get<Point_3>(&*intersection_result)) {
            // Intersection is a point
            return true;
        }
    }

    return false;
}

1. segmentConeIntersection Implementation using CGAL

Here's a more complete implementation of segmentConeIntersection using CGAL, along with explanations:

Geometry.hpp:

C++

#ifndef SLIC3R_GEOMETRY_HPP
#define SLIC3R_GEOMETRY_HPP

// ... other includes and declarations ...

// Include CGAL headers
#include <CGAL/Exact_predicates_inexact_constructions_kernel.h>
#include <CGAL/Segment_3.h>
#include <CGAL/Cone_3.h>
#include <CGAL/intersection.h>

namespace Slic3r {
namespace Geometry {

typedef CGAL::Exact_predicates_inexact_constructions_kernel K;
typedef K::Point_3 Point_3;
typedef K::Segment_3 Segment_3;
typedef K::Triangle_3 Triangle_3;
typedef K::Vector_3 Vector_3;
typedef K::Direction_3 Direction_3;
typedef K::Line_3 Line_3;
typedef K::FT FT;

// ... other functions ...

// Function to check intersection between a 3D line segment and a cone using CGAL
bool segmentConeIntersection(const Point3& p1, const Point3& p2, const Point3& nozzle_tip,
                             double nozzle_tip_radius, double nozzle_cone_angle, double nozzle_height);

} // namespace Geometry
} // namespace Slic3r

#endif // SLIC3R_GEOMETRY_HPP
Geometry.cpp:

C++

#include "Geometry.hpp"
#include <cmath>
#include <algorithm>

// Include CGAL headers
#include <CGAL/Exact_predicates_inexact_constructions_kernel.h>
#include <CGAL/Segment_3.h>
#include <CGAL/intersection.h>
#include <CGAL/Origin.h>
#include "PrintConfig.hpp"

namespace Slic3r {
namespace Geometry {

// ... other functions ...

bool segmentConeIntersection(const Point3& p1, const Point3& p2, const Point3& nozzle_tip,
    double nozzle_tip_radius, double nozzle_cone_angle, double nozzle_height) {
    try {
        // Create CGAL points for the segment
        K::Point_3 cp1(p1.x(), p1.y(), p1.z());
        K::Point_3 cp2(p2.x(), p2.y(), p2.z());
        Segment_3 segment(cp1, cp2);

        // Create CGAL points for the nozzle cone
        K::Point_3 c_nozzle_tip(nozzle_tip.x(), nozzle_tip.y(), nozzle_tip.z());

        // Calculate the apex of the cone (where the tip would be if the cone continued)
        FT cone_height_to_apex = nozzle_tip_radius / tan(deg2rad(nozzle_cone_angle / 2.0));

        // Define the direction vector of the cone axis (pointing upwards from the tip)
        Vector_3 cone_axis_direction(0, 0, 1);

        // Calculate the apex point of the cone
        K::Point_3 apex = c_nozzle_tip - cone_axis_direction * cone_height_to_apex;

        // Create a CGAL Cone
        // The radius at the base of the cone needs to be calculated considering the nozzle height
        FT base_radius = (nozzle_tip_radius + nozzle_height * tan(deg2rad(nozzle_cone_angle / 2.0)));

        // Create a CGAL Cone
        K::Cone_3 cone(apex, cone_axis_direction, deg2rad(nozzle_cone_angle / 2.0));

        // Check for intersection
        auto intersection_result = CGAL::intersection(segment, cone);

        // Check if an intersection occurred
        if (intersection_result) {
            // Further check based on the type of intersection
            if (const Segment_3* segment_result = boost::get<Segment_3>(&*intersection_result)) {
                // Intersection is a segment
                return true;
            }
            else if (const Point_3* point_result = boost::get<Point_3>(&*intersection_result)) {
                // Intersection is a point
                return true;
            }
        }
    }
    catch (const CGAL::Precondition_exception& e) {
        std::cerr << "CGAL Precondition Exception in segmentConeIntersection: " << e.what() << std::endl;
        // Handle the error (e.g., log, switch to planar slicing, etc.)
        return false;
    }
    catch (const std::exception& e) {
        std::cerr << "Exception in segmentConeIntersection: " << e.what() << std::endl;
        // Handle the error
        return false;
    }

    return false;
}

} // namespace Geometry
} // namespace Slic3r
Explanation:

Includes: Includes necessary CGAL headers:

<CGAL/Exact_predicates_inexact_constructions_kernel.h>: Defines the geometric kernel for exact predicates and inexact constructions.
<CGAL/Segment_3.h>: Defines the 3D segment type.
<CGAL/Cone_3.h>: Defines the 3D cone type.
<CGAL/intersection.h>: Provides intersection algorithms.
Kernel: Uses CGAL::Exact_predicates_inexact_constructions_kernel as the kernel. This kernel provides exact geometric predicates (to determine if points are on the same side of a line, for example) but uses inexact constructions (like creating a point at the intersection of two lines), which is generally faster but can have slight inaccuracies. For most slicing operations, the inexact constructions are acceptable, but you can switch to a kernel with exact constructions if higher precision is needed (though it will be slower).

Data Types: Defines type aliases for convenience:

Point_3, Segment_3, Vector_3, FT (for floating-point type).
segmentConeIntersection Function:

Input: Takes the endpoints of the segment (p1, p2), the nozzle tip position (nozzle_tip), the nozzle tip radius, the nozzle cone angle, and the nozzle height as input.
Create CGAL Objects:
Converts the input points to K::Point_3 objects.
Creates a K::Segment_3 object representing the line segment.
Creates a K::Cone_3 object representing the nozzle cone. The constructor takes the apex, direction, and the angle of the cone.
Intersection Check:
Calls CGAL::intersection(segment, cone) to compute the intersection between the segment and the cone. The result is stored in intersection_result.
The intersection_result is a boost::optional that will contain a value if there's an intersection.
Result Processing:
Checks if intersection_result has a value (meaning an intersection exists).
Uses boost::get to extract the intersection object. It could be either a K::Segment_3 or a K::Point_3. We return true if the intersection is either a point or a segment.
Error Handling: The try-catch block handles potential exceptions thrown by CGAL.
2. Error Handling

Geometry.cpp: The segmentConeIntersection function now includes a try-catch block to handle potential exceptions thrown by CGAL functions (e.g., CGAL::Precondition_exception if the input doesn't satisfy the preconditions of a function).
ConicalSlicer.cpp: In checkForCollision, if segmentConeIntersection returns false (no collision), you might want to add a log message or handle it in some way to indicate a potential issue.
General Error Handling: Throughout your code, consider adding:
try-catch blocks around operations that might throw exceptions.
Return values to indicate success or failure of functions.
Logging to record errors, warnings, and important events during slicing.
3. Spatial Data Structures (Octree Example)

Here's how you could integrate a simple octree for collision detection. We'll use a basic octree implementation for demonstration purposes.

A. Create Octree.hpp and Octree.cpp in src/libslic3r:

Octree.hpp:
C++

#ifndef SLIC3R_OCTREE_HPP
#define SLIC3R_OCTREE_HPP

#include <vector>
#include "Geometry.hpp"

namespace Slic3r {

    // Forward declaration of the bounding box class
    class BoundingBox;

    class Octree {
    public:
        Octree(const BoundingBox& bounds, int capacity = 4);
        ~Octree();

        void insert(const Geometry::Point_3& point);
        void queryRange(const Geometry::Point_3& center, double radius, std::vector<Geometry::Point_3>& result) const;
        void clear();

    private:
        struct Node {
            BoundingBox bounds;
            std::vector<Geometry::Point_3> points;
            Node* children[8]; // Eight children for an octree
            bool isLeaf;

            Node(const BoundingBox& b) : bounds(b), isLeaf(true) {
                for (int i = 0; i < 8; ++i) children[i] = nullptr;
            }
        };

        Node* root;
        int capacity; // Maximum number of points per node before subdividing

        void subdivide(Node* node);
        void queryRangeRecursive(Node* node, const Geometry::Point_3& center, double radius, std::vector<Geometry::Point_3>& result) const;
    };

} // namespace Slic3r

#endif // SLIC3R_OCTREE_HPP
Octree.cpp:
C++

#include "Octree.hpp"
#include "BoundingBox.hpp"
#include <algorithm>

namespace Slic3r {

    Octree::Octree(const BoundingBox& bounds, int nodeCapacity) : capacity(nodeCapacity) {
        root = new Node(bounds);
    }

    Octree::~Octree() {
        delete root;
    }

    void Octree::insert(const Geometry::Point_3& point) {
        insertRecursive(root, point);
    }

    void Octree::insertRecursive(Node* node, const Geometry::Point_3& point) {
        if (!node->bounds.contains(Point(point.x(), point.y())))
            return; // Point is outside the bounds of the node

        if (node->isLeaf) {
            node->points.push_back(point);
            if (node->points.size() > capacity) {
                subdivide(node);
            }
        }
        else {
            // Recursively insert into the appropriate child node
            for (int i = 0; i < 8; ++i) {
                if (node->children[i]->bounds.contains(Point(point.x(), point.y()))) {
                    insertRecursive(node->children[i], point);
                    break;
                }
            }
        }
    }

    void Octree::subdivide(Node* node) {
        // Create eight children
        Vec3f half_size = (node->bounds.max - node->bounds.min) / 2.0f;
        for (int i = 0; i < 8; ++i) {
            Vec3f child_min = node->bounds.min;
            if ((i & 1) != 0) child_min.x() += half_size.x();
            if ((i & 2) != 0) child_min.y() += half_size.y();
            if ((i & 4) != 0) child_min.z() += half_size.z();
            node->children[i] = new Node(BoundingBox(child_min, child_min + half_size));
        }

        // Distribute points to children
        for (const Geometry::Point_3& p : node->points) {
            for (int i = 0; i < 8; ++i) {
                if (node->children[i]->bounds.contains(Point(p.x(), p.y()))) {
                    insertRecursive(node->children[i], p);
                    break;
                }
            }
        }

        node->points.clear();
        node->isLeaf = false;
    }

    void Octree::queryRange(const Geometry::Point_3& center, double radius, std::vector<Geometry::Point_3>& result) const {
        queryRangeRecursive(root, center, radius, result);
    }

    void Octree::queryRangeRecursive(Node* node, const Geometry::Point_3& center, double radius, std::vector<Geometry::Point_3>& result) const {
        // Check if the node's bounding box intersects the query sphere
        if (!node->bounds.intersectsSphere(Point(center.x(), center.y()), center.z(), radius)) {
            return; // No intersection
        }

        if (node->isLeaf) {
            // If it's a leaf node, check each point
            for (const Geometry::Point_3& p : node->points) {
                if (Geometry::distance(Point(center.x(), center.y()), Point(p.x(), p.y())) <= radius) {
                    result.push_back(p);
                }
            }
        }
        else {
            // If it's not a leaf node, recursively query the children
            for (int i = 0; i < 8; ++i) {
                queryRangeRecursive(node->children[i], center, radius, result);
            }
        }
    }

    void Octree::clear() {
        delete root;
        root = new Node(root->bounds); // Recreate the root node with the same bounds
    }

} // namespace Slic3r

// ...

void ConicalSlicer::sliceLayerConically(Layer* layer, const PrintConfig& print_config) {
    // ...

    // Build the octree at the beginning of each layer
    // Define the bounding box for the octree
    BoundingBox bbox;

    // Iterate over all previous toolpaths to expand the bounding box
    for (const auto& layer_points : previous_toolpaths) {
        for (const auto& point : layer_points) {
            bbox.merge(Point(point.x(), point.y())); // Assuming 2D points for simplicity
        }
    }

    // Ensure the bounding box is valid before creating the octree
    if (!bbox.defined) {
        // Handle the case where the bounding box is not defined, 
        // possibly by setting default bounds or skipping octree creation
        std::cerr << "Warning: Bounding box not defined in sliceLayerConically." << std::endl;
        
        // For now, let's set some default bounds
        bbox.min = Point(-100, -100);
        bbox.max = Point(100, 100);
    }

    // Create and build the octree
    if (toolpath_octree) {
        delete toolpath_octree; // Clean up the old octree before creating a new one
        toolpath_octree = nullptr; // Reset the pointer
    }
    toolpath_octree = new Octree(bbox);

    for (const auto& layer_points : previous_toolpaths) {
        for (const Geometry::Point_3& point : layer_points) {
            toolpath_octree->insert(point);
        }
    }

    // ...

    // In checkForCollision:
    // Use the octree to find nearby points
    std::vector<Geometry::Point_3> nearby_points;
    toolpath_octree->queryRange(nozzle_tip, nozzle_tip_radius + nozzle_height * std::tan(Geometry::deg2rad




continue


2.0 Experimental Advanced. Lacks access to real-time info and some Gemini features.
C++

    // In checkForCollision:
    // Use the octree to find nearby points
    std::vector<Geometry::Point_3> nearby_points;
    toolpath_octree->queryRange(nozzle_tip, nozzle_tip_radius + nozzle_height * std::tan(Geometry::deg2rad(nozzle_cone_angle)), nearby_points);

    // Iterate through nearby points and check for collisions
    for (const Geometry::Point_3& p1 : nearby_points) {
        // Find the segment that this point belongs to
        bool foundSegment = false;
        for (size_t layer_idx = 0; layer_idx < previous_toolpaths.size(); ++layer_idx) {
            const auto& layer_points = previous_toolpaths[layer_idx];
            for (size_t i = 0; i < layer_points.size() - 1; ++i) {
                const Geometry::Point_3& seg_p1 = layer_points[i];
                const Geometry::Point_3& seg_p2 = layer_points[i + 1];

                // Check if p1 is one of the segment endpoints
                if (p1 == seg_p1 || p1 == seg_p2) {
                    // Check for intersection between the nozzle cone and the segment
                    if (Geometry::segmentConeIntersection(seg_p1, seg_p2, nozzle_tip, nozzle_tip_radius, nozzle_cone_angle, nozzle_height)) {
                        return true; // Collision detected
                    }
                    foundSegment = true;
                    break; // Found the segment for p1, no need to check further
                }
            }
            if (foundSegment) break;
        }
    }

    return false; // No collision
}

E. Add BoundingBox.hpp:

C++

#ifndef BOUNDINGBOX_HPP
#define BOUNDINGBOX_HPP

#include "Point.hpp"
#include "Vec.hpp"

namespace Slic3r {

class BoundingBox {
public:
    Point min;
    Point max;
    bool defined;

    BoundingBox();
    BoundingBox(const Point& min_pt, const Point& max_pt);
    BoundingBox(const Vec3f& min_pt, const Vec3f& max_pt);

    void merge(const Point& point);
    void merge(const Vec3f& point);
    void merge(const BoundingBox& other);

    bool contains(const Point& point) const;
    bool contains(const Vec3f& point) const;
    bool intersectsSphere(const Point& center, double z, double radius) const;

    Vec3f size() const;
    Point center() const;
};

} // namespace Slic3r

#endif // BOUNDINGBOX_HPP
F. Add BoundingBox.cpp:

C++

#include "BoundingBox.hpp"
#include <algorithm>
#include <limits>

namespace Slic3r {

BoundingBox::BoundingBox() : defined(false) {}

BoundingBox::BoundingBox(const Point& min_pt, const Point& max_pt)
    : min(min_pt), max(max_pt), defined(true) {}

BoundingBox::BoundingBox(const Vec3f& min_pt, const Vec3f& max_pt)
    : min(static_cast<coord_t>(min_pt.x()), static_cast<coord_t>(min_pt.y())),
      max(static_cast<coord_t>(max_pt.x()), static_cast<coord_t>(max_pt.y())),
      defined(true)
{
}

void BoundingBox::merge(const Point& point) {
    if (!defined) {
        min = point;
        max = point;
        defined = true;
    } else {
        min.x() = std::min(min.x(), point.x());
        min.y() = std::min(min.y(), point.y());
        max.x() = std::max(max.x(), point.x());
        max.y() = std::max(max.y(), point.y());
    }
}

void BoundingBox::merge(const Vec3f& point) {
    merge(Point(static_cast<coord_t>(point.x()), static_cast<coord_t>(point.y())));
}

void BoundingBox::merge(const BoundingBox& other) {
    if (!other.defined)
        return;
    if (!defined) {
        *this = other;
    } else {
        merge(other.min);
        merge(other.max);
    }
}

bool BoundingBox::contains(const Point& point) const {
    return defined &&
           point.x() >= min.x() && point.x() <= max.x() &&
           point.y() >= min.y() && point.y() <= max.y();
}

bool BoundingBox::contains(const Vec3f& point) const {
    return contains(Point(static_cast<coord_t>(point.x()), static_cast<coord_t>(point.y())));
}

bool BoundingBox::intersectsSphere(const Point& center, double z, double radius) const {
    // Check if the bounding box intersects with a sphere at a given z-height
    if (!defined)
        return false;

    // Find the closest point to the sphere's center on the bounding box
    Point closest_point;
    closest_point.x() = std::max(min.x(), std::min(center.x(), max.x()));
    closest_point.y() = std::max(min.y(), std::min(center.y(), max.y()));

    // Calculate the distance between the closest point and the sphere's center
    double distance_squared = std::pow(closest_point.x() - center.x(), 2) +
                              std::pow(closest_point.y() - center.y(), 2);

    // Check if the distance is less than or equal to the radius squared
    return distance_squared <= std::pow(radius, 2);
}

Vec3f BoundingBox::size() const {
    return max - min;
}

Point BoundingBox::center() const {
    return Point((min.x() + max.x()) / 2, (min.y() + max.y()) / 2);
}

} // namespace Slic3r

+ConicalSlicer::ConicalSlicer(const PrintConfig& print_config)
+    : nozzle_tip_radius(print_config.opt_float("nozzle_tip_radius")),
+      nozzle_cone_angle(print_config.opt_float("nozzle_cone_angle")),
+      nozzle_height(0.6),
+      toolpath_octree(nullptr)
+{
+    // The constructor now initializes the nozzle parameters using values from PrintConfig.
+    // Make sure these parameters are correctly loaded from the configuration in your Print object.
+}
+ConicalSlicer::~ConicalSlicer() {}

+void ConicalSlicer::sliceLayerConically(Layer* layer, const PrintConfig& print_config) {
+    // Retrieve conical slicing parameters
+    double cone_angle = print_config.opt_float("cone_angle");
+    double center_x = print_config.opt_float("cone_center_x");
+    double center_y = print_config.opt_float("cone_center_y");
+    double tip_radius = print_config.opt_float("nozzle_tip_radius");
+    double cone_angle_nozzle = print_config.opt_float("nozzle_cone_angle");
+
+    // Adjust layer height based on the conical method
+    // Iterate through regions in the layer
+    for (auto region : layer->regions()) {
+        // Iterate through perimeters
+        for (auto perimeter : region->perimeters()) {
+            // Create a copy of the perimeter points for modification
+            ExtrusionPath modified_perimeter = *perimeter;
+            // Iterate through each point of the perimeter
+            for (size_t i = 0; i < modified_perimeter.points.size(); ++i) {
+                auto& point = modified_perimeter.points[i];
+                //transform each point
+                Point3 transformed_point = transformToConical(
+                    Point3(point.x, point.y, layer->height),
+                    cone_angle,
+                    center_x,
+                    center_y,
+                    layer->height
+                );
+                // Before adding the point, check for collisions
+                Geometry::Point_3 nozzle_center = Geometry::Point_3(transformed_point.x(), transformed_point.y(), transformed_point.z() + nozzle_height / 2.0);
+                if (checkForCollision(nozzle_center, tip_radius, cone_angle_nozzle, nozzle_height, previous_toolpaths)) {
+                    // Handle collision (for now, just skip the point)
+                    // You might want to implement more sophisticated handling later
+                    //remove point from perimeter
+                    modified_perimeter.points.erase(modified_perimeter.points.begin() + i);
+                    --i; // Adjust the index after erasing
+                    continue;
+                }
+
+                // Update the point in the perimeter
+                point.x = transformed_point.x();
+                point.y = transformed_point.y();
+
+                // Adjust the layer height based on the transformation
+                double radius = std::sqrt(std::pow(point.x - center_x, 2) + std::pow(point.y - center_y, 2));
+                layer->height = calculateConicalLayerHeight(radius, cone_angle);
+
+                // Add the point to the collision detection system
+                addToolpathPoint(transformed_point);
+            }
+
+            // Replace the original perimeter with the modified one
+            *perimeter = modified_perimeter;
+
+            // Adjust extrusion for this perimeter
+            double scale_factor = std::cos(Geometry::deg2rad(cone_angle)); // Example scale factor
+            for (auto& loop : perimeter->loops) {
+                adjustExtrusion(&loop, scale_factor);
+            }
+        }
+
+        // Similar adjustments can be made for infill and supports
+        for (auto& infill : region->infill_paths()) {
+            for (size_t i = 0; i < infill.points.size(); ++i) {
+                auto& point = infill.points[i];
+                Point3 transformed_point = transformToConical(Point3(point.x, point.y, layer->height), cone_angle, center_x, center_y, layer->height);
+
+                // Check for collisions
+                Geometry::Point_3 nozzle_center = Geometry::Point_3(transformed_point.x(), transformed_point.y(), transformed_point.z() + nozzle_height / 2.0);
+                if (checkForCollision(nozzle_center, tip_radius, cone_angle_nozzle, nozzle_height, previous_toolpaths)) {
+                    // Handle collision
+                    //remove point from infill
+                    infill.points.erase(infill.points.begin() + i);




continue


2.0 Experimental Advanced. Lacks access to real-time info and some Gemini features.
C++

                    --i; // Adjust the index
                    continue;
                }
+
+                point.x = transformed_point.x();
+                point.y = transformed_point.y();
+
+                // Add the point to the collision detection system
+                addToolpathPoint(transformed_point);
+            }
+        }
+    }
+
+    // Shift the toolpath points for the next layer
+    if (previous_toolpaths.size() >= MAX_LAYERS_TO_CHECK) {
+        previous_toolpaths.erase(previous_toolpaths.begin());
+    }
+    previous_toolpaths.push_back({}); // Add an empty layer for the new points
+
+    // Build the octree at the beginning of each layer
+    // Define the bounding box for the octree
+    BoundingBox bbox;
+
+    // Iterate over all previous toolpaths to expand the bounding box
+    for (const auto& layer_points : previous_toolpaths) {
+        for (const auto& point : layer_points) {
+            bbox.merge(Point(point.x(), point.y())); // Assuming 2D points for simplicity
+        }
+    }
+
+    // Ensure the bounding box is valid before creating the octree
+    if (!bbox.defined) {
+        // Handle the case where the bounding box is not defined, 
+        // possibly by setting default bounds or skipping octree creation
+        std::cerr << "Warning: Bounding box not defined in sliceLayerConically." << std::endl;
+
+        // For now, let's set some default bounds
+        bbox.min = Point(-100, -100);
+        bbox.max = Point(100, 100);
+    }
+
+    // Create and build the octree
+    if (toolpath_octree) {
+        delete toolpath_octree; // Clean up the old octree before creating a new one
+        toolpath_octree = nullptr; // Reset the pointer
+    }
+    toolpath_octree = new Octree(bbox);
+
+    for (const auto& layer_points : previous_toolpaths) {
+        for (const Geometry::Point_3& point : layer_points) {
+            toolpath_octree->insert(point);
+        }
+    }
+}
+
+Point3 ConicalSlicer::transformToConical(const Point3& point, double cone_angle, double center_x, double center_y, double layer_height_mm) {
+    // Calculate radius from the center
+    double radius = std::sqrt(std::pow(point.x - center_x, 2) + std::pow(point.y - center_y, 2));
+
+    // Calculate conical layer height
+    double conical_z = layer_height_mm + calculateConicalLayerHeight(radius, cone_angle);
+
+    // Keep x and y unchanged for this example, but you'll likely modify them
+    // based on the cone's geometry and the desired toolpath.
+    double transformed_x = point.x;
+    double transformed_y = point.y;
+
+    return Point3(transformed_x, transformed_y, conical_z);
+}
+
+double ConicalSlicer::calculateConicalLayerHeight(double radius, double cone_angle) {
+    // Calculate the layer height based on the cone angle and radius
+    return radius * std::tan(Geometry::deg2rad(cone_angle));
+}
+
+void ConicalSlicer::adjustExtrusion(ExtrusionLoop* loop, double scale_factor) {
+    // Adjust the extrusion for each segment of the loop based on the scale factor
+    for (ExtrusionPath& path : loop->paths) {
+        for (size_t i = 0; i < path.points.size(); ++i) {
+            // Retrieve the original extrusion amount
+            double original_extrusion = path.e;
+
+            // Calculate the scaled extrusion amount
+            double scaled_extrusion = original_extrusion * scale_factor;
+
+            // Update the extrusion amount in the path
+            path.e = scaled_extrusion;
+        }
+    }
+}
+
+bool ConicalSlicer::checkForCollision(const Geometry::Point_3& nozzle_tip, double nozzle_tip_radius, double nozzle_cone_angle, double nozzle_height,
+    const std::vector<std::vector<Geometry::Point_3>>& previous_toolpaths) {
+    // Use the octree to find nearby points
+    std::vector<Geometry::Point_3> nearby_points;
+    toolpath_octree->queryRange(nozzle_tip, nozzle_tip_radius + nozzle_height * std::tan(Geometry::deg2rad(nozzle_cone_angle)), nearby_points);
+
+    // Iterate through nearby points and check for collisions
+    for (const Geometry::Point_3& p1 : nearby_points) {
+        // Find the segment that this point belongs to
+        bool foundSegment = false;
+        for (size_t layer_idx = 0; layer_idx < previous_toolpaths.size(); ++layer_idx) {
+            const auto& layer_points = previous_toolpaths[layer_idx];
+            for (size_t i = 0; i < layer_points.size() - 1; ++i) {
+                const Geometry::Point_3& seg_p1 = layer_points[i];
+                const Geometry::Point_3& seg_p2 = layer_points[i + 1];
+
+                // Check if p1 is one of the segment endpoints
+                if (p1 == seg_p1 || p1 == seg_p2) {
+                    // Check for intersection between the nozzle cone and the segment
+                    if (Geometry::segmentConeIntersection(seg_p1, seg_p2, nozzle_tip, nozzle_tip_radius, nozzle_cone_angle, nozzle_height)) {
+                        return true; // Collision detected
+                    }
+                    foundSegment = true;
+                    break; // Found the segment for p1, no need to check further
+                }
+            }
+            if (foundSegment) break;
+        }
+    }
+
+    return false; // No collision
+}
+
+void ConicalSlicer::addToolpathPoint(const Point3& point) {
+    if (!previous_toolpaths.empty()) {
+        previous_toolpaths.back().push_back(Geometry::Point_3(point.x(), point.y(), point.z()));
+    }
+}
+
+} // namespace Slic3r

16. Smoothing.cpp:

C++

#include "Smoothing.hpp"
#include <vector>

namespace Slic3r {

void smoothToolpath(ExtrusionPath* path, int window_size) {
    if (path->points.size() < window_size) {
        return; // Not enough points to smooth
    }

    std::vector<Point> smoothed_points;
    smoothed_points.reserve(path->points.size());

    for (size_t i = 0; i < path->points.size(); ++i) {
        Point smoothed_point;
        int count = 0;

        for (int j = std::max(0, static_cast<int>(i) - window_size / 2);
             j <= std::min(static_cast<int>(path->points.size()) - 1, static_cast<int>(i) + window_size / 2);
             ++j) {
            smoothed_point += path->points[j];
            count++;
        }

        smoothed_points.push_back(smoothed_point / count);
    }

    path->points = smoothed_points;
}

} // namespace Slic3r
17. Octree.hpp:

C++

#ifndef SLIC3R_OCTREE_HPP
#define SLIC3R_OCTREE_HPP

#include <vector>
#include "Geometry.hpp"
#include "BoundingBox.hpp"

namespace Slic3r {

    class Octree {
    public:
        Octree(const BoundingBox& bounds, int capacity = 4);
        ~Octree();

        void insert(const Geometry::Point_3& point);
        void queryRange(const Geometry::Point_3& center, double radius, std::vector<Geometry::Point_3>& result) const;
        void clear();

    private:
        struct Node {
            BoundingBox bounds;
            std::vector<Geometry::Point_3> points;
            Node* children[8]; // Eight children for an octree
            bool isLeaf;

            Node(const BoundingBox& b) : bounds(b), isLeaf(true) {
                for (int i = 0; i < 8; ++i) children[i] = nullptr;
            }
        };

        Node* root;
        int capacity; // Maximum number of points per node before subdividing

        void insertRecursive(Node* node, const Geometry::Point_3& point);
        void subdivide(Node* node);
        void queryRangeRecursive(Node* node, const Geometry::Point_3& center, double radius, std::vector<Geometry::Point_3>& result) const;
    };

} // namespace Slic3r

#endif // SLIC3R_OCTREE_HPP
18. Octree.cpp:

C++

#include "Octree.hpp"
#include <algorithm>

namespace Slic3r {

    Octree::Octree(const BoundingBox& bounds, int nodeCapacity) : capacity(nodeCapacity) {
        root = new Node(bounds);
    }

    Octree::~Octree() {
        deleteNode(root);
    }

    void Octree::deleteNode(Node* node) {
        if (node) {
            if (!node->isLeaf) {
                for (int i = 0; i < 8; ++i) {
                    deleteNode(node->children[i]);
                }
            }
            delete node;
        }
    }

    void Octree::insert(const Geometry::Point_3& point) {
        insertRecursive(root, point);
    }

    void Octree::insertRecursive(Node* node, const Geometry::Point_3& point) {
        if (!node->bounds.contains(Point(point.x(), point.y())))
            return; // Point is outside the bounds of the node

        if (node->isLeaf) {
            node->points.push_back(point);
            if (node->points.size() > capacity) {
                subdivide(node);
            }
        }
        else {
            // Recursively insert into the appropriate child node
            for (int i = 0; i < 8; ++i) {
                if (node->children[i]->bounds.contains(Point(point.x(), point.y()))) {
                    insertRecursive(node->children[i], point);
                    break;
                }
            }
        }
    }

    void Octree::subdivide(Node* node) {
        // Create eight children
        Vec3f half_size = (node->bounds.max - node->bounds.min) / 2.0f;
        for (int i = 0; i < 8; ++i) {
            Vec3f child_min = node->bounds.min;
            if ((i & 1) != 0) child_min.x() += half_size.x();
            if ((i & 2) != 0) child_min.y() += half_size.y();
            if ((i & 4) != 0) child_min.z() += half_size.z();
            node->children[i] = new Node(BoundingBox(child_min, child_min + half_size));
        }

        // Distribute points to children
        for (const Geometry::Point_3& p : node->points) {
            for (int i = 0; i < 8; ++i) {
                if (node->children[i]->bounds.contains(Point(p.x(), p.y()))) {
                    insertRecursive(node->children[i], p);
                    break;
                }
            }
        }

        node->points.clear();
        node->isLeaf = false;
    }

    void Octree::queryRange(const Geometry::Point_3& center, double radius, std::vector<Geometry::Point_3>& result) const {
        queryRangeRecursive(root, center, radius, result);
    }

    void Octree::queryRangeRecursive(Node* node, const Geometry::Point_3& center, double radius, std::vector<Geometry::Point_3>& result) const {
        // Check if the node's bounding box intersects the query sphere
        if (!node->bounds.intersectsSphere(Point(center.x(), center.y()), center.z(), radius)) {
            return; // No intersection
        }

        if (node->isLeaf) {
            // If it's a leaf node, check each point
            for (const Geometry::Point_3& p : node->points) {
                if (Geometry::distance(Point(center.x(), center.y()), Point(p.x(), p.y())) <= radius) {
                    result.push_back(p);
                }
            }
        }
        else {
            // If it's not a leaf node, recursively query the children
            for (int i = 0; i < 8; ++i) {
                queryRangeRecursive(node->children[i], center, radius, result);
            }
        }
    }

    void Octree::clear() {
        delete root;
        root = new Node(root->bounds); // Recreate the root node with the same bounds
    }

} // namespace Slic3r
