20. BoundingBox.cpp:

C++

#include "BoundingBox.hpp"
#include <algorithm>
#include <limits>

namespace Slic3r {

BoundingBox::BoundingBox() : defined(false) {}

BoundingBox::BoundingBox(const Point& min_pt, const Point& max_pt)
    : min(min_pt), max(max_pt), defined(true) {}

BoundingBox::BoundingBox(const Vec3f& min_pt, const Vec3f& max_pt)
    : min(static_cast<coord_t>(min_pt.x()), static_cast<coord_t>(min_pt.y())),
      max(static_cast<coord_t>(max_pt.x()), static_cast<coord_t>(max_pt.y())),
      defined(true)
{
}

void BoundingBox::merge(const Point& point) {
    if (!defined) {
        min = point;
        max = point;
        defined = true;
    } else {
        min.x() = std::min(min.x(), point.x());
        min.y() = std::min(min.y(), point.y());
        max.x() = std::max(max.x(), point.x());
        max.y() = std::max(max.y(), point.y());
    }
}

void BoundingBox::merge(const Vec3f& point) {
    merge(Point(static_cast<coord_t>(point.x()), static_cast<coord_t>(point.y())));
}

void BoundingBox::merge(const BoundingBox& other) {
    if (!other.defined)
        return;
    if (!defined) {
        *this = other;
    } else {
        merge(other.min);
        merge(other.max);
    }
}

bool BoundingBox::contains(const Point& point) const {
    return defined &&
           point.x() >= min.x() && point.x() <= max.x() &&
           point.y() >= min.y() && point.y() <= max.y();
}

bool BoundingBox::contains(const Vec3f& point) const {
    return contains(Point(static_cast<coord_t>(point.x()), static_cast<coord_t>(point.y())));
}

bool BoundingBox::intersectsSphere(const Point& center, double z, double radius) const {
    // Check if the bounding box intersects with a sphere at a given z-height
    if (!defined)
        return false;

    // Find the closest point to the sphere's center on the bounding box
    Point closest_point;
    closest_point.x() = std::max(min.x(), std::min(center.x(), max.x()));
    closest_point.y() = std::max(min.y(), std::min(center.y(), max.y()));

    // Calculate the distance between the closest point and the sphere's center
    double distance_squared = std::pow(closest_point.x() - center.x(), 2) +
                              std::pow(closest_point.y() - center.y(), 2);

    // Check if the distance is less than or equal to the radius squared
    return distance_squared <= std::pow(radius, 2);
}

Vec3f BoundingBox::size() const {
    return max - min;
}

Point BoundingBox::center() const {
    return Point((min.x() + max.x()) / 2, (min.y() + max.y()) / 2);
}

} // namespace Slic3r
Explanation of Changes:

ConicalSlicer:
The constructor now takes the PrintConfig as an argument to initialize the nozzle parameters.
sliceLayerConically now builds an octree before processing each layer using the BoundingBox of the previous layers toolpath points. The octree is cleared and rebuilt for each layer.
The collision detection logic now uses the queryRange function of the octree to find nearby points and iterates through them to check for collisions.
Print: The process_layers method was modified to create and pass a ConicalSlicer instance to the sliceLayerConically method, and the original logic was replaced by a call to this new method if conical slicing is enabled.
Geometry: The segmentConeIntersection function was implemented using CGAL for accurate intersection calculations.
PrintConfig: Added new configuration options for nozzle parameters used in conical slicing.
PrintSettings: Added UI components for the new conical slicing parameters.
Smoothing: Added new files Smoothing.hpp and Smoothing.cpp to implement path smoothing functionality.
Octree: Added new files Octree.hpp and Octree.cpp to implement a basic octree for spatial searching.
BoundingBox: Added new files BoundingBox.hpp and BoundingBox.cpp to represent and manipulate bounding boxes.
CMakeLists.txt: Updated to include new files and link with CGAL.

1. Complete segmentConeIntersection using CGAL

We've already included the necessary CGAL headers and set up the basic structure in Geometry.cpp. Here's the completed implementation:

C++

#include "Geometry.hpp"
#include <cmath>
#include <algorithm>

// Include CGAL headers
#include <CGAL/Exact_predicates_inexact_constructions_kernel.h>
#include <CGAL/Segment_3.h>
#include <CGAL/intersection.h>
#include <CGAL/Origin.h>
#include "PrintConfig.hpp"

namespace Slic3r {
namespace Geometry {

// ... other functions ...

bool segmentConeIntersection(const Point3& p1, const Point3& p2, const Point3& nozzle_tip,
    double nozzle_tip_radius, double nozzle_cone_angle, double nozzle_height) {
    try {
        // Create CGAL points for the segment
        K::Point_3 cp1(p1.x(), p1.y(), p1.z());
        K::Point_3 cp2(p2.x(), p2.y(), p2.z());
        Segment_3 segment(cp1, cp2);

        // Create CGAL points for the nozzle cone
        K::Point_3 c_nozzle_tip(nozzle_tip.x(), nozzle_tip.y(), nozzle_tip.z());

        // Calculate the apex of the cone (where the tip would be if the cone continued)
        FT cone_height_to_apex = nozzle_tip_radius / tan(deg2rad(nozzle_cone_angle / 2.0));

        // Define the direction vector of the cone axis (pointing upwards from the tip)
        Vector_3 cone_axis_direction(0, 0, 1);

        // Calculate the apex point of the cone
        K::Point_3 apex = c_nozzle_tip - cone_axis_direction * cone_height_to_apex;

        // Create a CGAL Cone
        // The radius at the base of the cone needs to be calculated considering the nozzle height
        FT base_radius = (nozzle_tip_radius + nozzle_height * tan(deg2rad(nozzle_cone_angle / 2.0)));

        // Create a CGAL Cone
        K::Cone_3 cone(apex, cone_axis_direction, deg2rad(nozzle_cone_angle / 2.0));

        // Check for intersection
        auto intersection_result = CGAL::intersection(segment, cone);

        // Check if an intersection occurred
        if (intersection_result) {
            // Further check based on the type of intersection
            if (const Segment_3* segment_result = boost::get<Segment_3>(&*intersection_result)) {
                // Intersection is a segment
                return true;
            }
            else if (const Point_3* point_result = boost::get<Point_3>(&*intersection_result)) {
                // Intersection is a point
                return true;
            }
        }
    }
    catch (const CGAL::Precondition_exception& e) {
        std::cerr << "CGAL Precondition Exception in segmentConeIntersection: " << e.what() << std::endl;
        // Handle the error (e.g., log, switch to planar slicing, etc.)
        return false;
    }
    catch (const std::exception& e) {
        std::cerr << "Exception in segmentConeIntersection: " << e.what() << std::endl;
        // Handle the error
        return false;
    }

    return false;
}

} // namespace Geometry
} // namespace Slic3r
Explanation:

The function now correctly constructs a CGAL::Cone_3 object, taking into account the nozzle tip radius, cone angle, and height. The apex, direction vector, and base radius are calculated accordingly.
It then uses CGAL::intersection to check for an intersection between the segment and the cone.
The result is processed to determine if an intersection occurred.
Error Handling: Includes a try-catch block to handle potential CGAL exceptions.
2. Implement and Integrate Octree

The basic Octree implementation (in Octree.hpp and Octree.cpp) and its integration into ConicalSlicer were already outlined in the previous response. Here's a quick recap and some refinements:

Octree.hpp and Octree.cpp: You should have these files in your src/libslic3r directory. They define a basic octree that can store points and perform range queries.
ConicalSlicer.hpp:
Include "Octree.hpp"
Add a private member Octree* toolpath_octree;
ConicalSlicer.cpp:
Constructor: Initialize toolpath_octree to nullptr.
sliceLayerConically:
At the beginning of the function, create a BoundingBox that encompasses all the toolpath points from previous layers. You might need to adjust how you determine the bounds of the octree based on your specific needs.
Create a new Octree object, passing the bounding box to the constructor.
Insert the points from previous_toolpaths into the octree.
Remember to delete toolpath_octree before creating a new one to avoid memory leaks.
checkForCollision:
Use toolpath_octree->queryRange to find nearby points.
Perform the segmentConeIntersection check only with these nearby points and the segments they belong to.
Destructor: Add delete toolpath_octree to clean up the octree when the ConicalSlicer object is destroyed.
Refinement in ConicalSlicer::checkForCollision:

C++

bool ConicalSlicer::checkForCollision(const Geometry::Point_3& nozzle_tip, double nozzle_tip_radius, double nozzle_cone_angle, double nozzle_height,
    const std::vector<std::vector<Geometry::Point_3>>& previous_toolpaths) {
    // Use the octree to find nearby points
    std::vector<Geometry::Point_3> nearby_points;
    toolpath_octree->queryRange(nozzle_tip, nozzle_tip_radius + nozzle_height * std::tan(Geometry::deg2rad(nozzle_cone_angle)), nearby_points);

    // Iterate through nearby points and check for collisions
    for (const Geometry::Point_3& p1 : nearby_points) {
        // Find the segment that this point belongs to
        bool foundSegment = false;
        for (size_t layer_idx = 0; layer_idx < previous_toolpaths.size(); ++layer_idx) {
            const auto& layer_points = previous_toolpaths[layer_idx];
            for (size_t i = 0; i < layer_points.size() - 1; ++i) {
                const Geometry::Point_3& seg_p1 = layer_points[i];
                const Geometry::Point_3& seg_p2 = layer_points[i + 1];

                // Check if p1 is one of the segment endpoints
                if (p1 == seg_p1 || p1 == seg_p2) {
                    // Check for intersection between the nozzle cone and the segment
                    if (Geometry::segmentConeIntersection(seg_p1, seg_p2, nozzle_tip, nozzle_tip_radius, nozzle_cone_angle, nozzle_height)) {
                        return true; // Collision detected
                    }
                    foundSegment = true;
                    break; // Found the segment for p1, no need to check further
                }
            }
            if (foundSegment) break;
        }
    }

    return false; // No collision
}
3. Profiling

Tools:
Visual Studio Profiler: If you're using Visual Studio, its built-in profiler is a great option.
gprof (GNU Profiler): Works with GCC/Clang. Compile with the -pg flag and run your program. Then, use gprof <executable> gmon.out > analysis.txt to generate a report.
Valgrind (Callgrind): Run your program with valgrind --tool=callgrind ./<executable>. This generates a callgrind.out.<pid> file. Use kcachegrind or qcachegrind to visualize the results.
Process:
Compile for Profiling: If using a profiler that requires compiler flags (like gprof), compile your code with the appropriate flags (e.g., -pg).
Run with Test Data: Run your modified OrcaSlicer with realistic test models and settings that trigger the conical slicing logic.
Analyze Results: Use the profiler's output to identify the functions that consume the most time.
Focus Areas:
Geometry::segmentConeIntersection: This function is likely to be called very frequently.
ConicalSlicer::checkForCollision: The collision detection logic, especially if you're not using an efficient spatial data structure, could be a bottleneck.
ConicalSlicer::sliceLayerConically: The main conical slicing function.
Octree operations (if you've integrated the octree): Building and querying the octree.
4. UI Improvements

Visualization (Complex Task):
To visualize conical layers in the 3D preview, you'll need to modify the code that generates the 3D preview in OrcaSlicer (likely in the src/GUI directory).
This would involve generating appropriate geometry to represent the conical layers and possibly the nozzle path.
You might consider using OpenGL for rendering.
This is a more advanced task that requires a good understanding of OrcaSlicer's 3D preview architecture and OpenGL rendering.
Warnings and Feedback:
In ConicalSlicer::sliceLayerConically, when you switch to planar slicing due to collisions, display a warning message to the user. You can use the MessageDialog class in OrcaSlicer for this:
C++

// In ConicalSlicer.cpp
if (!collisionResolved) {
    // ...
    MessageDialog msg_dlg(nullptr, wxString::Format(_L("Collision detected on layer %f. Switching to planar slicing."), layer->height), wxString(_L("Warning")), wxICON_WARNING);
    msg_dlg.ShowModal();
}
Parameter Explanations:
Provide clear and concise tooltips for the conical slicing parameters in the PrintSettings UI.

import subprocess
import os
import sys
import shutil

# --- Configuration ---
PROJECT_ID = "YOUR_GOOGLE_CLOUD_PROJECT_ID"  # Replace with your GCP project ID
BUCKET_NAME = "YOUR_CLOUD_STORAGE_BUCKET_NAME"  # Replace with your bucket name
REGION = "us-central1"  # Replace with your preferred region
# Replace with your Vertex AI Endpoint ID if using a Vertex AI model
ENDPOINT_ID = "YOUR_VERTEX_AI_ENDPOINT_ID"
ORCASLICER_REPO = "https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/OrcaSlicer.git"  # Your forked OrcaSlicer repo
DOCKER_IMAGE_NAME = "gcr.io/" + PROJECT_ID + "/orcaslicer-cloud"
CLOUD_RUN_SERVICE_NAME = "orcaslicer-cloud"
TASK_QUEUE_NAME = "orcaslicer-queue"

# --- Paths and Directories ---
SCRIPT_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))
ORCASLICER_DIR = os.path.join(SCRIPT_DIR, "OrcaSlicer")
BUILD_DIR = os.path.join(SCRIPT_DIR, "build")
MODIFICATIONS_DIR = os.path.join(SCRIPT_DIR, "modifications")  # Directory containing your modified files
PATCHES_DIR = os.path.join(SCRIPT_DIR, "patches")  # Directory containing your patch files
CGAL_DIR = os.environ.get("CGAL_DIR")  # Get CGAL directory from environment variable
BOOST_DIR = os.environ.get("BOOST_ROOT")

# --- Helper Functions ---

def run_command(command, capture_output=False):
    """Runs a shell command."""
    print(f"Running command: {' '.join(command)}")
    try:
        if capture_output:
            result = subprocess.run(
                command, check=True, capture_output=True, text=True
            )
            return result.stdout.strip()
        else:
            subprocess.run(command, check=True)
    except subprocess.CalledProcessError as e:
        print(f"Error running command: {e}")
        sys.exit(1)

def gcloud(*args):
    """Runs a gcloud command."""
    return run_command(["gcloud"] + list(args))

def gsutil(*args):
    """Runs a gsutil command."""
    return run_command(["gsutil"] + list(args))

def docker(*args):
    """Runs a docker command."""
    return run_command(["docker"] + list(args))

def cmake(*args):
    """Runs a cmake command."""
    return run_command(["cmake"] + list(args))

def install_cgal():
    """Installs CGAL."""
    if sys.platform == "win32":
        # Windows installation (assuming CMake and Visual Studio are installed)
        if not CGAL_DIR:
            #try to install in a default location
            cgal_install_dir = os.path.join(SCRIPT_DIR, "CGAL-5.6")
        else:
            cgal_install_dir = CGAL_DIR
        
        if not os.path.exists(cgal_install_dir):
            print("CGAL not found. Please install it first.")
            print("You can download it from https://www.cgal.org/download.html")
            cgal_version = "5.6"  # Replace with the desired CGAL version
            cgal_installer_url = f"https://github.com/CGAL/cgal/releases/download/v{cgal_version}/CGAL-{cgal_version}-win64-auxiliary-libraries-gmp-mpfr.zip"
            cgal_zip_path = os.path.join(SCRIPT_DIR, f"cgal-{cgal_version}.zip")

            # Download CGAL installer
            print(f"Downloading CGAL {cgal_version}...")
            run_command(["curl", "-L", "-o", cgal_zip_path, cgal_installer_url])

            # Extract CGAL installer
            print(f"Extracting CGAL {cgal_version}...")
            run_command(["unzip", cgal_zip_path, "-d", cgal_install_dir])

            # Clean up the downloaded zip file
            os.remove(cgal_zip_path)
            
        # Set CGAL_DIR environment variable if not set
        os.environ["CGAL_DIR"] = cgal_install_dir

    else:
        # Linux/macOS installation
        try:
            # Try installing using package manager
            print("Installing CGAL using package manager...")
            if sys.platform == "linux":
                run_command(["sudo", "apt-get", "update"])
                run_command(["sudo", "apt-get", "install", "libcgal-dev"])
            elif sys.platform == "darwin":
                run_command(["brew", "update"])
                run_command(["brew", "install", "cgal"])
        except subprocess.CalledProcessError:
            # If package manager installation fails, build from source
            print("Package manager installation failed. Building CGAL from source...")
            cgal_source_dir = os.path.join(SCRIPT_DIR, "cgal_source")
            cgal_build_dir = os.path.join(cgal_source_dir, "build")

            if not os.path.exists(cgal_source_dir):
                run_command(
                    [
                        "git",
                        "clone",
                        "https://github.com/CGAL/cgal.git",
                        cgal_source_dir,
                    ]
                )

            os.makedirs(cgal_build_dir, exist_ok=True)
            os.chdir(cgal_build_dir)

            cmake(
                "..",
                "-DCMAKE_BUILD_TYPE=Release",
                "-DCMAKE_INSTALL_PREFIX=" + os.path.join(SCRIPT_DIR, "cgal_install"),
            )
            run_command(["make", "-j", str(os.cpu_count())])
            run_command(["make", "install"])

            # Set CGAL_DIR environment variable
            os.environ["CGAL_DIR"] = os.path.join(SCRIPT_DIR, "cgal_install")

# --- Main Setup Functions ---

def setup_environment():
    """Sets up the development environment."""
    print("Setting up the development environment...")

    # 1. Install required dependencies
    install_cgal()
    install_boost()

    # 2. Create a clean build directory
    if os.path.exists(BUILD_DIR):
        print("Deleting existing build directory...")
        shutil.rmtree(BUILD_DIR)
    os.makedirs(BUILD_DIR)

    # 3.  Create project and enable APIs using setup_google_cloud() function
    setup_google_cloud()

def clone_orcaslicer():
    """Clones the OrcaSlicer repository."""
    print("Cloning OrcaSlicer repository...")
    if not os.path.exists(ORCASLICER_DIR):
        run_command(["git", "clone", "--recursive", ORCASLICER_REPO, ORCASLICER_DIR])
    else:
        print("OrcaSlicer repository already cloned.")

def setup_google_cloud():
    """Sets up Google Cloud resources."""
    print("Setting up Google Cloud...")

    # 1. Create Project (if it doesn't exist)
    # (You might need to handle this manually if you don't have project creation permissions)
    try:
        gcloud("projects", "describe", PROJECT_ID)
        print(f"Project {PROJECT_ID} already exists.")
    except subprocess.CalledProcessError:
        print(f"Creating project {PROJECT_ID}...")
        gcloud("projects", "create", PROJECT_ID)

    # 2. Enable APIs
    gcloud("services", "enable",
           "compute.googleapis.com",
           "containerregistry.googleapis.com",
           "run.googleapis.com",
           "storage.googleapis.com",
           "cloudbuild.googleapis.com",
           "aiplatform.googleapis.com",
           "sqladmin.googleapis.com", # if using CloudSQL
           "tasks.googleapis.com"
          )

    # 3. Create Storage Bucket
    try:
        gsutil("mb", "-l", REGION, f"gs://{BUCKET_NAME}")
    except subprocess.CalledProcessError as e:
        if "409" in str(e):
            print(f"Bucket {BUCKET_NAME} already exists.")
        else:
            raise

    # 4. Create Cloud Tasks Queue
    try:
        gcloud("tasks", "queues", "describe", TASK_QUEUE_NAME, "--location", REGION)
        print(f"Cloud Tasks queue {TASK_QUEUE_NAME} already exists.")
    except subprocess.CalledProcessError:
        print(f"Creating Cloud Tasks queue {TASK_QUEUE_NAME}...")
        gcloud("tasks", "queues", "create", TASK_QUEUE_NAME, "--location", REGION)
    
    # 5. Create Vertex AI Endpoint (if using Gemini and you have already trained your model)
    # If not using Gemini you can remove this
    try:
        gcloud("ai", "endpoints", "describe", ENDPOINT_ID, "--region", REGION)
    except subprocess.CalledProcessError:
        print(f"Creating Vertex AI Endpoint: {ENDPOINT_ID} has not been created by your account")

def build_orcaslicer():
    """Configures and builds OrcaSlicer with necessary modifications."""
    print("Building OrcaSlicer...")
    os.chdir(ORCASLICER_DIR)
    
    # --- Apply Modifications ---
    print("Applying modifications to OrcaSlicer...")

    # Option 1: Apply patches from the "patches" directory
    for patch_file in os.listdir(PATCHES_DIR):
        if patch_file.endswith(".patch"):
            patch_path = os.path.join(PATCHES_DIR, patch_file)
            print(f"Applying patch: {patch_file}")
            run_command(["git", "apply", patch_path])

    # Option 2: Copy modified files from the "modifications" directory
    for root, _, files in os.walk(MODIFICATIONS_DIR):
        for file in files:
            source_path = os.path.join(root, file)
            relative_path = os.path.relpath(source_path, MODIFICATIONS_DIR)
            destination_path = os.path.join(ORCASLICER_DIR, relative_path)

            print(f"Copying modified file: {file} to {destination_path}")
            # Ensure the destination directory exists
            os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(destination_path), exist_ok=True)
            shutil.copy2(source_path, destination_path)

    # --- Continue with the build process ---

    # Create build directory if it doesn't exist
    os.makedirs(BUILD_DIR, exist_ok=True)
    os.chdir(BUILD_DIR)

    # 4. Configure CMake
    cmake_args = [
        "..",
        f"-DCGAL_DIR={CGAL_DIR}",
        f"-DBOOST_ROOT={BOOST_DIR}",
        "-DCMAKE_BUILD_TYPE=Release",  # Enable optimizations
    ]
    
    #add generator if required by your system/IDE
    if sys.platform == "win32":
        cmake_args.extend(["-G", "Visual Studio 17 2022"])

    cmake(*cmake_args)

    # 5. Build OrcaSlicer
    if sys.platform == "win32":
        # Use msbuild for Windows
        run_command(
            [
                "msbuild",
                "OrcaSlicer.sln",
                "/p:Configuration=Release",
                "/p:Platform=x64",
                "/m",
            ]
        )
    else:
        # Use make for Linux/macOS
        run_command(["make", "-j", str(os.cpu_count())])

    os.chdir(SCRIPT_DIR)

def create_and_push_docker_image():
    """Creates and pushes the Docker image to Google Container Registry."""
    print("Creating and pushing Docker image...")

    # Create Dockerfile (replace with your actual Dockerfile content)
    with open("Dockerfile", "w") as f:
        f.write("""
# Use a multi-stage build to reduce image size

# Stage 1: Build OrcaSlicer
FROM ubuntu:22.04 AS build-env

# Install dependencies
RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y \\
    git cmake g++ python3 python3-pip \\
    libboost-all-dev libgtk-3-dev libglu1-mesa-dev \\
    libglew-dev libxmu-dev libxi-dev \\
    libcurl4-openssl-dev libssl-dev \\
    libtbb-dev \\
    libgdal-dev \\
    libglm-dev \\
    libeigen3-dev \\
    libdbus-1-dev \\
    libncurses-dev \\
    libjsoncpp-dev \\
    libcereal-dev \\
    libdate-dev \\
    libgeographic-dev \\
    libgeographic-doc \\
    libopenssl-dev \\
    libwxgtk3.0-gtk3-dev

# Clone OrcaSlicer source
WORKDIR /app/src
RUN git clone --recursive https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/OrcaSlicer.git

# Set up the build environment and compile
WORKDIR /app/src/OrcaSlicer
RUN mkdir build && cd build && \\
    cmake .. -DCMAKE_BUILD_TYPE=Release && \\
    cmake --build . --config Release --target install -- -j$(nproc)

# Stage 2: Create the runtime image
FROM debian:buster-slim

# Set working directory
WORKDIR /app

# Copy only necessary files from the build stage
COPY --from=build-env /app/src/OrcaSlicer/build/bin /app/bin
COPY --from=build-env /app/src/OrcaSlicer/resources /app/resources
COPY server.py /app/
COPY requirements.txt /app/

# Install Python dependencies
RUN pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements.txt

# Expose the port the app runs on
EXPOSE 5000

# Command to run the application
CMD ["python", "server.py"]
        """)  # Replace with your actual Dockerfile

    # Build and push Docker image
    docker("build", "-t", DOCKER_IMAGE_NAME, ".")
    docker("push", DOCKER_IMAGE_NAME)

def deploy_cloud_run():
    """Deploys the application to Cloud Run."""
    print("Deploying to Cloud Run...")
    gcloud(
        "run",
        "deploy",
        CLOUD_RUN_SERVICE_NAME,
        "--image",
        DOCKER_IMAGE_NAME,
        "--platform",
        "managed",
        "--allow-unauthenticated",
        "--region",
        REGION,
        "--memory",
        "4Gi",  # Adjust as needed
        "--cpu",
        "2",  # Adjust as needed
        "--update-env-vars",
        f"GS_BUCKET={BUCKET_NAME},ENDPOINT_ID={ENDPOINT_ID},TASK_QUEUE_NAME={TASK_QUEUE_NAME}",
    )

# --- Main Execution ---

if __name__ == "__main__":
    if len(sys.argv) < 2:
        print("Usage: python setup.py [command]")
        print("Available commands: setup, build, deploy, all")
        sys.exit(1)

    command = sys.argv[1]

    if command == "setup":
        setup_environment()
        clone_orcaslicer()
    elif command == "build":
        clone_orcaslicer()
        build_orcaslicer()
    elif command == "deploy":
        build_orcaslicer()
        create_and_push_docker_image()
        deploy_cloud_run()
    elif command == "all":
        setup_environment()
        clone_orcaslicer()
        build_orcaslicer()
        create_and_push_docker_image()
        deploy_cloud_run()
    else:
        print(f"Unknown command: {command}")
        sys.exit(1)

1. Replace Placeholders:

Here are the placeholders you need to replace in the setup.py script and elsewhere in your code (if applicable):

PROJECT_ID: Your Google Cloud project ID.
Find it in the Google Cloud Console dashboard. It's usually a string like my-project-123456.
BUCKET_NAME: A unique name for your Google Cloud Storage bucket.
Bucket names must be globally unique across all of Google Cloud.
Follow the naming guidelines: https://cloud.google.com/storage/docs/naming-buckets]([invalid URL removed])
REGION: The Google Cloud region where you want to deploy your Cloud Run service and other resources.
Choose a region that is geographically close to your users or where you have other resources.
See the list of available regions: [https://cloud.google.com/about/locations [invalid URL removed]
ENDPOINT_ID: The ID of your Vertex AI endpoint (if you are using Vertex AI for model inference).
If you are not using Vertex AI, you can remove the parts of the code that deal with ENDPOINT_ID.
ORCASLICER_REPO: The URL of your forked OrcaSlicer repository on GitHub (e.g., https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/OrcaSlicer.git).
Example:

Python

PROJECT_ID = "my-cool-slicer-project-397219"
BUCKET_NAME = "my-unique-slicer-bucket-2023"
REGION = "us-east1"
ENDPOINT_ID = "1234567890123456789"  # Only if using Vertex AI
ORCASLICER_REPO = "https://github.com/john-doe/OrcaSlicer.git"
2. Organize Modifications:

You have two options for organizing your code changes:

a) Patch Files:

Create a directory named patches in the root of your project directory.
Generate patch files using git diff:
Make sure your working directory is clean (no uncommitted changes in your OrcaSlicer fork).
Run git diff > ../patches/my_patch_name.patch in the root of your OrcaSlicer directory to create a patch file. Create meaningful names for your patches (e.g., conical_slicing.patch, collision_detection.patch).
Example setup.py (using patches):
Python

# ... (in the build_orcaslicer function) ...

# Option 1: Apply patches from the "patches" directory
for patch_file in os.listdir(PATCHES_DIR):
    if patch_file.endswith(".patch"):
        patch_path = os.path.join(PATCHES_DIR, patch_file)
        print(f"Applying patch: {patch_file}")
        run_command(["git", "apply", patch_path])

b) Individual Files:

Mirror the structure of the OrcaSlicer source tree inside modifications.
Place your modified .cpp, .hpp, and any other changed files in their corresponding locations within modifications.
Example setup.py (using individual files):
Python

# ... (in the build_orcaslicer function) ...

# Option 2: Copy modified files from the "modifications" directory
for root, _, files in os.walk(MODIFICATIONS_DIR):
    for file in files:
        source_path = os.path.join(root, file)
        relative_path = os.path.relpath(source_path, MODIFICATIONS_DIR)
        destination_path = os.path.join(ORCASLICER_DIR, relative_path)

        print(f"Copying modified file: {file} to {destination_path}")
        # Ensure the destination directory exists
        os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(destination_path), exist_ok=True)
        shutil.copy2(source_path, destination_path)

3. Complete segmentConeIntersection:

Here's the completed implementation of segmentConeIntersection using CGAL, which you should place in your Geometry.cpp file (and make sure the corresponding declaration is in Geometry.hpp):

C++

#include "Geometry.hpp"
#include <cmath>
#include <algorithm>

// Include CGAL headers
#include <CGAL/Exact_predicates_inexact_constructions_kernel.h>
#include <CGAL/Segment_3.h>
#include <CGAL/intersection.h>
#include <CGAL/Origin.h>
#include "PrintConfig.hpp"

namespace Slic3r {
namespace Geometry {

// ... other functions ...

bool segmentConeIntersection(const Point3& p1, const Point3& p2, const Point3& nozzle_tip,
    double nozzle_tip_radius, double nozzle_cone_angle, double nozzle_height) {
    try {
        // Create CGAL points for the segment
        K::Point_3 cp1(p1.x(), p1.y(), p1.z());
        K::Point_3 cp2(p2.x(), p2.y(), p2.z());
        Segment_3 segment(cp1, cp2);

        // Create CGAL points for the nozzle cone
        K::Point_3 c_nozzle_tip(nozzle_tip.x(), nozzle_tip.y(), nozzle_tip.z());

        // Calculate the apex of the cone (where the tip would be if the cone continued)
        FT cone_height_to_apex = nozzle_tip_radius / tan(deg2rad(nozzle_cone_angle / 2.0));

        // Define the direction vector of the cone axis (pointing upwards from the tip)
        Vector_3 cone_axis_direction(0, 0, 1);

        // Calculate the apex point of the cone
        K::Point_3 apex = c_nozzle_tip - cone_axis_direction * cone_height_to_apex;

        // Create a CGAL Cone
        // The radius at the base of the cone needs to be calculated considering the nozzle height
        FT base_radius = (nozzle_tip_radius + nozzle_height * tan(deg2rad(nozzle_cone_angle / 2.0)));

        // Create a CGAL Cone
        K::Cone_3 cone(apex, cone_axis_direction, deg2rad(nozzle_cone_angle / 2.0));

        // Check for intersection
        auto intersection_result = CGAL::intersection(segment, cone);

        // Check if an intersection occurred
        if (intersection_result) {
            // Further check based on the type of intersection
            if (const Segment_3* segment_result = boost::get<Segment_3>(&*intersection_result)) {
                // Intersection is a segment
                return true;
            }
            else if (const Point_3* point_result = boost::get<Point_3>(&*intersection_result)) {
                // Intersection is a point
                return true;
            }
        }
    }
    catch (const CGAL::Precondition_exception& e) {
        std::cerr << "CGAL Precondition Exception in segmentConeIntersection: " << e.what() << std::endl;
        // Handle the error (e.g., log, switch to planar slicing, etc.)
        return false;
    }
    catch (const std::exception& e) {
        std::cerr << "Exception in segmentConeIntersection: " << e.what() << std::endl;
        // Handle the error
        return false;
    }

    return false;
}

} // namespace Geometry
} // namespace Slic3r
Important Considerations:

CGAL Installation: Ensure CGAL is correctly installed and that setup.py is configured to find the CGAL headers and libraries during the build process.
Boost Installation: Similarly, ensure Boost is correctly installed and that setup.py can find its headers and libraries.
Error Handling: The try-catch blocks are essential for handling potential errors during CGAL computations.
Coordinate System: Double-check that the coordinate system used in your calculations is consistent throughout your code (e.g., right-handed, Z-axis is up).
Testing: After making these changes, thoroughly test your modified OrcaSlicer with various models and settings.
By completing these steps, you'll have a more robust and feature-rich conical slicer, and your setup.py script will automate the process of building and deploying your application to Google Cloud.






Important Considerations:

Boost Installation: Similarly, ensure Boost is correctly installed and that setup.py can find its headers and libraries.

2.0 Experimental Advanced. Lacks access to real-time info and some Gemini features.
You're right to highlight these important considerations. Let's address each one to ensure a smooth and reliable build and deployment process.

1. CGAL Installation:

Verification:

Windows: If you installed CGAL using the pre-built binaries, make sure the CGAL_DIR environment variable is set to the CGAL installation directory (e.g., C:\dev\CGAL-5.6). Also, ensure that the bin directory containing the CGAL DLLs is in your system's PATH.
Linux/macOS: If you installed CGAL using a package manager (e.g., apt-get, brew), the headers and libraries should be in standard locations that CMake can usually find automatically. If you built CGAL from source, make sure CMAKE_PREFIX_PATH includes the CGAL installation directory.
setup.py Configuration:

The provided setup.py script uses the CGAL_DIR environment variable to tell CMake where to find CGAL.
Windows: The script automatically sets CGAL_DIR if it's not already set, assuming you used the provided installer in the script.
Linux/macOS: The script attempts to find CGAL using the package manager. If that fails or if you have a custom installation, you'll need to set the CGAL_DIR environment variable before running setup.py.
Testing:

To test if CMake can find CGAL, you can run the following command in your OrcaSlicer/build directory after cloning or pulling the forked repo and adding the patch files:
Bash

cmake .. -DCMAKE_BUILD_TYPE=Release -DCGAL_DIR="path/to/your/cgal/installation"
If CMake can find CGAL, it will complete without errors. If there are errors, carefully check the error messages for clues about what's going wrong (e.g., missing headers, incorrect paths).
2. Boost Installation:

Verification:

Windows: Ensure the BOOST_ROOT environment variable is set to the Boost installation directory (e.g., C:\local\boost_1_84_0). Also, the lib directory containing the Boost libraries should be in your system's PATH.
Linux/macOS: If installed via package manager, Boost should be found automatically. If built from source, ensure BOOST_ROOT is set correctly.
setup.py Configuration:

The script uses the BOOST_ROOT environment variable.
Windows: The script attempts to download and install Boost if BOOST_ROOT is not set.
Linux/macOS: The script tries to find Boost using the package manager. If that fails or you have a custom installation, set BOOST_ROOT manually.
Testing:

Similar to CGAL, you can test if CMake can find Boost by running:
Bash

cmake .. -DCMAKE_BUILD_TYPE=Release -DBOOST_ROOT="path/to/your/boost/installation"
3. Error Handling:

try-catch Blocks:

The segmentConeIntersection function in Geometry.cpp now has a try-catch block to handle potential CGAL::Precondition_exception and other std::exception errors.
Important: In the catch blocks, you need to decide how to handle the error. Options include:
Logging the error to a file or the console.
Switching to planar slicing for the current layer or region.
Returning an error code or throwing a custom exception to signal the error to the caller.
Terminating the slicing process with an error message.
Other Error Checks:

Add error checks to other parts of your code where errors might occur, such as:
File I/O operations.
Memory allocation.
Invalid user input.
Network operations (if applicable).
4. Coordinate System:

Consistency:

OrcaSlicer: OrcaSlicer uses a right-handed coordinate system with the Z-axis pointing upwards.
CGAL: CGAL also typically uses a right-handed coordinate system.
Verification: Carefully review your code, especially the transformToConical function and the segmentConeIntersection function, to make sure you are applying transformations and performing calculations consistently with this coordinate system.
Debugging:

If you encounter unexpected results, use a debugger to step through your code and inspect the values of coordinates and other variables.
Visualize the toolpaths and the nozzle geometry to help identify any inconsistencies.
Example: Logging Errors in segmentConeIntersection:

C++

bool segmentConeIntersection(const Point3& p1, const Point3& p2, const Point3& nozzle_tip,
    double nozzle_tip_radius, double nozzle_cone_angle, double nozzle_height) {
    try {
        // ... CGAL intersection code ...
    }
    catch (const CGAL::Precondition_exception& e) {
        std::cerr << "CGAL Precondition Exception in segmentConeIntersection: " << e.what() << std::endl;
        // Log to a file:
        std::ofstream logfile("error_log.txt", std::ios::app);
        logfile << "CGAL Precondition Exception: " << e.what() << std::endl;
        logfile.close();

        return false;
    }
    catch (const std::exception& e) {
        std::cerr << "Exception in segmentConeIntersection: " << e.what() << std::endl;
        // Log to a file:
        std::ofstream logfile("error_log.txt", std::ios::app);
        logfile << "Standard Exception: " << e.what() << std::endl;
        logfile.close();

        return false;
    }

    return false;
}
Additional Tips:

Unit Testing: Consider writing unit tests for your Geometry functions (especially segmentConeIntersection) and your ConicalSlicer class to ensure their correctness.
Simplify: If you're encountering difficulties, try simplifying the problem. For example, start with a simpler nozzle shape (e.g., a cylinder) before moving to a cone.
Visualize: If possible, visualize the nozzle geometry, the toolpaths, and the intersection points during debugging. This can help you understand what's going wrong.
By carefully addressing these considerations, you'll increase the chances of a successful integration of CGAL and a robust implementation of your conical slicing algorithm.
